Washing Hands When Tilting the Vessel is Not Possible
Provides practical rules for washing hands before wudu when the vessel cannot be tilted.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three methods for washing hands before wudu when the water vessel cannot be tilted and identify when the water becomes musta'mal.

Core Idea
Water purity is protected: never insert the palm unless necessary, or the water becomes musta'mal.

When performing wudu, we must ensure the water in the vessel remains pure and usable. The classical Hanafi texts provide a detailed procedure for washing the hands before wudu when the water container cannot be tilted. Depending on the size of the vessel and the availability of a smaller scooping tool, the method changes. This lesson walks through those cases and highlights the key fiqh principle: avoiding wastage and contamination of water.

Guided Path
1
Identify the baseline ruling
Recognize that the primary concern is not to contaminate the water by inserting impure hands. The default is to tilt the vessel; if not possible, alternative methods are used.
This concern stems from the principle of preserving the purity of water (taharat al-ma').
2
Classify the vessel size
Determine whether the vessel is small and liftable, or large and cannot be tilted. Also note whether a smaller vessel is available.
The text gives three scenarios: small vessel, large vessel with small vessel, large vessel without small vessel.
3
Apply the appropriate method
For a small vessel, lift it with the left hand and pour over the right, then switch. For a large vessel with a small vessel, scoop water with the small vessel. For a large vessel without a small vessel, use the left fingers (without the palm) to scoop and pour.
In the last case, the fingers are kept together and the palm is not inserted.
4
Recognize the consequence of exceeding necessity
If one inserts the full palm into the water when it is not needed, the water becomes musta'mal (used) and is no longer valid for wudu.
This is a key point: exceeding the necessary action renders the water used.
5
Summarize the sunnah nature
The washing of hands before wudu is a sunnah, but the method must be followed to avoid making water musta'mal. If the sunnah is omitted, wudu remains valid.
The ruling is sunnah, not wajib, except if the hands are najis.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإذا لم يمكن إمالة الإناء يدخل أصابع يسراه الخالية عن نجاسة متحققة ويصب على كفه اليمنى حتى ينقيها، ثم يدخل اليمنى ويغسل يسراه وإن زاد على قدر الضرورة فأدخل الكف صار الماء مستعملاً قوله: (وإذا لم يمكن إمالة الإناء) كيفية الغسل على ما ذكره أصحاب المذهب إنه إذا كان الإناء صغيراً يمكن رفعه لا يدخل يده فيه، بل يرفعه بشماله، ويصب على كفه اليمنى، فيغسلها ثلاثاً، ثم يأخذ الإناء بيمينه ويصب على كفه اليسرى فيغسلها ثلاثاً وإن كان الإناء كبيراً بحيث لا تمكن إمالته ، فإن كان معه إناء صغير رفع من الماء بذلك الإناء، وغسل يديه كما بينا، وإن لم يكن معه إناء صغير يدخل أصابع يده اليسرى مضمومة دون الكف ويرفع الماء، ويصب على كفه اليمنى، ويدلك الأصابع بعضها ببعض، يفعل ذلك ثلاثاً، ثم يدخل يده اليمني في الإناء بالغاً ما بلغ إن شاء الله، ويفعل باليسرى كذلك اهـ.
And if it is not possible to tilt the vessel, he inserts the fingers of his left hand that are free from certain impurity and pours onto his right palm until he cleans it, then he inserts the right [hand] and washes his left. And if he exceeds the necessary amount and inserts the palm, the water becomes musta'mal (used). His statement: (And if tilting the vessel is not possible) - the method of washing according to the madhhab scholars: if the vessel is small and can be lifted, he does not insert his hand into it, but lifts it with his left and pours onto his right palm, washing it three times, then takes the vessel with his right and pours onto his left palm, washing it three times. If the vessel is large such that tilting is not possible, if he has a small vessel, he scoops water with that vessel and washes his hands as described. If he has no small vessel, he inserts the fingers of his left hand together without the palm and lifts water, pours onto his right palm, rubs the fingers together, doing that three times, then inserts his right hand into the vessel as far as it goes, God willing, and does likewise with the left, etc.
Source pages p. 65

Commentary
This passage details the practical procedure for washing the hands before wudu when one cannot tilt the water vessel (e.g., a large pot). The basic rule is to avoid contaminating the water in the vessel by inserting impure hands. The method depends on the size of the vessel: for a small liftable vessel, one lifts it with the left hand and pours over the right, then switches. For a large vessel that cannot be tilted, one uses a smaller vessel to scoop water, or if none, uses the left fingers (not the full palm) to scoop and pour over the right hand, rubbing the fingers to clean them. The last step may involve inserting the hand into the vessel after cleaning. The text also notes that if one inserts the full palm, the water becomes musta'mal (used water, no longer fit for wudu). This ruling shows the meticulous attention to preventing water from becoming impure or used in wudu.

Key Terms
إمالة الإناء (imalat al-ina'): Tilting the water vessel to pour water without inserting the hand.
مستعمل (musta'mal): Used water that has already been employed for ritual purification, not valid for further wudu.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
When tilting the vessel is not possible, avoid inserting the palm unnecessarily to prevent the water from becoming musta'mal; use alternative methods depending on vessel size.

Intention and Musta'mal Water: The Intra-Hanafi Refinement
Intra-Hanafi dispute on the condition for musta'mal water

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition under which water becomes musta'mal when the hand is inserted, and distinguish between washing and scooping intentions.

Core Idea
Water becomes musta'mal only by intending washing, not by mere insertion.

The simple rule in Maraqi al-Falah states that inserting the hand beyond necessity makes water musta'mal. However, Al-Khaniyyah introduces a critical refinement: the outcome depends on intention. This lesson examines the intra-Hanafi dispute and the reconciled position that intention determines the water's status.

Guided Path
1
Identify the apparent ruling from the matn
The matn states 'صار الماء مستعملاً' (the water becomes musta'mal) when the hand is inserted beyond necessity, without mentioning intention.
This is the baseline position that students must recognize.
2
Identify the counter ruling from Al-Khaniyyah
Al-Khaniyyah explicitly states that if the hand is inserted for scooping (i'tiraf), the water does not become musta'mal.
Note the condition 'للإعتراف' (for scooping) that introduces intention.
3
Analyze the difference in condition
The difference is the presence or absence of intention. The matn appears unconditional; Al-Khaniyyah conditions the ruling on the purpose of insertion.
4
Apply the reconciliation from Al-Durr
Al-Durr resolves the dispute by explicitly stating: if one intends washing, water becomes musta'mal; if scooping, it does not.
This is the mufta bihi (operative) position.
5
Note the practical consequence: scope of musta'mal water
Even when intention is washing, only the water that contacts the hand becomes musta'mal, not the entire mass, as mentioned by al-Sayyid.
This preserves the purity of most of the water.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (صار الماء مستعملاً) مخالف لما في الخانية، ونصها المحدث، أو الجنب إذا أدخل يده في الماء للاعتراف، وليس عليها نجاسة لا يفسد الماء، وكذا إذا وقع الكوز في الجب، وأدخل يده إلى المرفق لا . يصير الماء مستعملاً اهـ وتقييده في الخانية بالاعتراف أي بنيته يفيد أنه إذا نوى الغسل الماء مستعملاً ويه صرح في الدر حيث قال : فلو أدخل الكف إن أراد الغسل صار الماء مستعملاً، وإن أراد الإعتراف لا اهـ واعلم أن المحكوم عليه بالاستعمال عند إرادة الغسل هو الملاقي ليده لا كل الماء ذكره السيد ومعنى الإغتراف: نقل الماء من نحو الإناء، ثم إذا صار في یده نوی به التطهير
His statement: (the water becomes musta'mal) opposes what is in Al-Khaniyyah. Its text: If a hadath person or a junub inserts his hand into water for scooping (al-i'tiraf) and there is no impurity on it, the water does not become impure. Similarly, if a pitcher falls into a well and he inserts his hand up to the elbow, the water does not become musta'mal. The restriction in Al-Khaniyyah to scooping, i.e., by intention, indicates that if he intends washing, the water becomes musta'mal. This is clearly stated in Al-Durr: 'If he inserts the palm, if he intends washing, the water becomes musta'mal; if he intends scooping, it does not.' Know that the water judged as musta'mal when intending washing is only the portion that contacts his hand, not all the water, as mentioned by al-Sayyid. The meaning of al-ightiraf is transferring water from the vessel, then when it is in his hand, he intends purification with it.
Source pages p. 66

Commentary
This passage clarifies a specific point about musta'mal (used) water. The Matn in Maraqi al-Falah stated that if one inserts his hand beyond necessity, the water becomes musta'mal. Al-Tahtawi notes that this ruling contradicts what is in Al-Khaniyyah, which says that water does not become musta'mal if the purpose is scooping (i'tiraf) rather than washing. The resolution is that the ruling depends on intention: if one intends to wash (ghusl) with the water, it becomes musta'mal; if one intends only to scoop (ightiraf), it does not. Furthermore, even if it becomes musta'mal, only the water that directly contacts the hand is rendered musta'mal, not the entire mass of water. This distinction is important for practical wudu: the water used for scooping remains pure and suitable for use. The term al-i'tiraf (scooping) means transferring water from the vessel to the hand with the intention of using it for purification.

Key Terms
ماء مستعمل (ma' musta'mal): Water that has been used for wudu or ghusl and is no longer pure for use in wudu.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Whenever the hand touches water
B) Only if the hand is inserted with the intention of washing
C) Only if the hand is impure
D) Only if the water is less than two qullahs

Key Takeaway
Water becomes musta'mal only when the hand is inserted with the intention of washing; scooping intention leaves it pure.

The Ruling on Tasmiyah at the Start of Wudu
Discusses the ruling on tasmiyah at wudu start with intra-Hanafi disagreement and timing rule.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the majority Hanafi ruling on saying Bismillah at the start of wudu, explain the intra-Hanafi disagreement about its legal status, and apply the timing rule that it must occur at the beginning to fulfill the sunnah.

Core Idea
Saying Bismillah at wudu start is sunnah mu'akkadah; if missed, it cannot be recovered because wudu is one continuous act.

This lesson explores the ruling of tasmiyah (saying 'Bismillah') at the beginning of wudu. While many Hanafi authorities consider it an emphatic sunnah (sunnah mu'akkadah), some view it as merely mustahabb (recommended), and a minority even hold it wajib (obligatory). The passage also clarifies a key timing rule: tasmiyah must be uttered at the very start; if forgotten, saying it mid-wudu does not fulfill the sunnah. Understanding this distinction helps you apply the correct legal categorization in practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its potential rulings
The act is saying 'Bismillah' (tasmiyah) at the start of wudu. The passage discusses whether it is sunnah mu'akkadah, mustahabb, or wajib. Note the different views within the Hanafi school.
The majority position is sunnah mu'akkadah; al-Hidayah says mustahabb; al-Kamal says wajib.
2
Examine the hadith evidence and its interpretation
The primary proof is the hadith: 'لا صلاة لمن لا وضوء له ولا وضوء لمن لم يذكر اسم الله عليه' (No prayer for one with no wudu, and no wudu for one who does not mention Allah's name). Scholars interpret the negation differently: some say it negates validity (thus wajib), but the Hanafi majority interpret it as negation of perfection (thus sunnah or mustahabb).
Al-Marghinani and others considered the hadith hasan due to multiple chains, supporting the sunnah ruling.
3
Understand the intra-Hanafi opinions
The passage mentions that Al-Mabsut, Muhit Radi al-Din, Al-Tuhfa, al-Quduri, al-Tahawi, and al-Marghinani count it among the emphatic sunan. Al-Hidayah considers the soundest view as mustahabb, possibly due to perceived weakness of the hadith. Al-Kamal argued for obligation by analogy to the obligation of al-Fatiha.
The mufta bihi (relied-upon ruling) is sunnah mu'akkadah, as indicated by al-Tahtawi.
4
Apply the timing rule: wudu as a single act
If one forgets tasmiyah at the start and remembers during wudu, saying it then does not earn the sunnah because wudu is a single act ('amal wahid). This is contrasted with eating, where each mouthful is an independent act, so tasmiyah can be said mid-meal to earn the sunnah for that and subsequent mouthfuls.
Even if the sunnah is missed, saying it during wudu is still mandub (recommended) to avoid leaving wudu devoid of dhikr.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والتسمية (ابتداء حتى لو نسيها فتذكرها في خلاله، وسمى لا تحصل له السنة بخلاف الأكل لأن الوضوء عمل واحد وكل لقمة فعل مستأنف لقوله : من توضأ وذكر يصير قوله: (والتسمية ابتداء) عدها من السنن المؤكدة هو ما في المبسوط، ومحيط رضى الدين والتحفة وغيرها واختاره القدوري والطحاوي وصاحب الكافي وصححه المرغيناني لقوله : لا صلاة لمن لا ضوء له ولا وضوء لمن لم يذكر اسم الله عليه رواه أبو داود والترمذي والحاكم، وهو محمول على نفي الكمال، وقال في الهداية : الأصح أنها مستحبة وكأن وجهه ضعف الحديث والأظهر أنه لا ينزل عن درجة الحسن لاعتضاده بكثرة الطرق والشواهد فكان حجة حتى أن الكمال أثبت به الوجوب، كما أن . وجوب الفاتحة ثبت بمثله، وأما تعيين كونها في الإبتداء. فدليله ما روى عن عائشة كان رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم إذا مس طهوره الله تعالى ثم يفرغ الماء على بدنه قوله : (لا تحصل له السنة) وفي السراج أنه يأتي بها لئلا يخلو وضؤه عنها، ومثله في الجوهرة أي ليكون آتيا بالمندوب، وإن فاتته السنة كما في الدر، وقالوا : إنّها عند غسل كل عضو مندوبة ذكره السيد قوله : (بخلاف الأكل) فإنه إذا أتى بها أثناءه تحصل السنة في الماضي والباقي كما ذكره الحلبي متعقباً الكمال في قوله : إنما تحصل السنة في الباقي فقط. قوله : لقوله صلى الله عليه وسلم الخ) الأولى في الاستدلال ما ذكره آنفاً.
And the tasmiyah (saying Bismillah) is at the beginning, so if he forgets it and remembers during it and says it, he does not get the sunnah, unlike eating, because wudu is one act and every mouthful is an independent act. Due to his saying: 'Whoever performs wudu and mentions [Allah]...' His statement: (Tasmiyah at the beginning) - counting it among the emphatic sunan is what is in Al-Mabsut, Muhit Radi al-Din, Al-Tuhfa, etc., and it was chosen by al-Quduri, al-Tahawi, the author of Al-Kafi, and al-Marghinani authenticated it, due to his saying: 'There is no prayer for one who has no wudu, and no wudu for one who does not mention the name of Allah upon it' (narrated by Abu Dawud, al-Tirmidhi, and al-Hakim), and it is interpreted as negation of perfection. Al-Hidayah said: The soundest view is that it is mustahabb, as if its basis is the weakness of the hadith. But the apparent view is that it is not lower than hasan because it is supported by many chains and witnesses, so it is an argument. Indeed, al-Kamal established obligation by it, just as the obligation of al-Fatiha is established by similar evidence. As for specifying that it is at the beginning, its evidence is what is narrated from A'isha: 'When the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) touched his purification, he would mention Allah then pour water on his body.' His statement: (He does not obtain the sunnah) - and in Al-Siraj, he comes with it so that his wudu is not devoid of it, and similar in Al-Jawhara, i.e., to be performing the mandub, even if the sunnah is missed, as in Al-Durr. They said: It is mandub when washing each limb, as mentioned by al-Sayyid. His statement: (Unlike eating) - for if he brings it during it, the sunnah is obtained for the past and the remaining, as mentioned by al-Halabi commenting on al-Kamal's statement that it is obtained only for the remaining. His statement: (Due to his saying) - the first in adducing evidence is what was mentioned earlier.
Source pages p. 66

Commentary
This passage discusses the ruling of saying 'Bismillah' (tasmiyah) at the beginning of wudu. The author explains that it is considered a sunnah mu'akkadah (emphatic sunnah) by many Hanafi authorities, based on the hadith 'لا صلاة لمن لا وضوء له ولا وضوء لمن لم يذكر اسم الله عليه' (No prayer for one who has no wudu, and no wudu for one who does not mention Allah's name). However, some weak the hadith, so Al-Hidayah considers it mustahabb. The majority, including al-Marghinani, affirm its hasan grade due to multiple chains, and some even consider it wajib (obligatory), analogizing to the obligation of reciting al-Fatiha. The specific timing is at the beginning, as narrated from A'isha. If one forgets and remembers mid-wudu, saying it then does not earn the sunnah for the whole wudu, because wudu is considered a single act, unlike eating where each mouthful is independent. The passage also notes that if the sunnah is missed, one may still say it to gain reward (mandub), as it is mandub at each limb according to some. The comparison with eating clarifies the legal principle: in wudu, the tasmiyah must be at the start to fulfill the sunnah; if missed, it cannot be recovered later.

Key Terms
التسمية (al-tasmiyah): Uttering 'Bismillah' (in the name of Allah) at the start of wudu.
السنة المؤكدة (al-sunnah al-mu'akkadah): Emphatic sunnah; an act that the Prophet consistently performed and recommended, but omitting it does not invalidate the act.
المستحبة (al-mustahabbah): Recommended; an act that is rewarded but omitting it is not disliked.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the majority Hanafi ruling on saying Bismillah at the start of wudu?
A) It is wajib (obligatory).
B) It is sunnah mu'akkadah (emphatic sunnah).
C) It is mustahabb (recommended).
D) It is mubah (permissible).

Key Takeaway
Saying 'Bismillah' at the start of wudu is a sunnah mu'akkadah; it must be said at the beginning to earn the specific sunnah, and if forgotten, saying it later does not compensate for the sunnah, though it remains a recommended act.

Washing Hands from a Vessel Upon Waking: Intention and Used Water
Ruling with proof on washing hands upon waking and the effect of intention on used water.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on washing hands upon waking and distinguish when water becomes musta'mal based on intention.

Core Idea
Intention determines whether water becomes musta'mal: scooping does not nullify, washing does.

This passage from Hashiyat al-Tahtawi on Maraqi al-Falah addresses the sunnah of washing hands upon waking and the critical role of intention in determining whether water becomes musta'mal. It provides the practical method for different vessel sizes and reconciles apparent contradictions in earlier Hanafi texts by emphasizing that the intention at the moment of inserting the hand (washing vs. scooping) is decisive.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act being ruled upon? It is the washing of hands upon waking from sleep. Determine the hukm level: is it fard, wajib, or sunnah? Note the proof cited.
The text mentions the hadith 'he does not know where his hand spent the night' as the basis.
2
Locate the dalil and trace the wajh al-dalalah
The dalil is the hadith from Bukhari and Muslim. Analyze how the phrase 'la yadri ayna batat yadahu' provides the reasoning (ta'lil) for the sunnah: the possibility of impurity justifies washing to avoid contaminating the vessel.
The dalil is ahad, so the ruling is sunnah, not fard.
3
Note the ikhtilaf with Imam Ahmad
Imam Ahmad restricts the sunnah to night sleep only. Understand his basis: the hadith specifies 'batat' (spent the night). The Hanafi position includes day sleep because the reason (ta'lil) is general.
This is a valid scholarly difference.
4
Analyze the intra-Hanafi reconciliation on musta'mal
The text points to an apparent contradiction between al-Khaniyyah and al-Durr. The resolution is that intention matters: if one inserts the hand intending to wash (ghusl), the water becomes musta'mal; if intending to scoop (ightiraf), it does not.
This is the mufta bihi position.
5
Apply the ruling to practical scenarios
Consider different vessel sizes and the proper method. Understand that only the water contacting the hand becomes musta'mal, not the entire body of water.
The method for small vs large vessels is detailed in the passage.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إمالة الإناء يدخل أصابع يسراه الخالية عن نجاسة متحققة ويصب على كفه اليمنى حتى ينقيها، ثم يدخل اليمنى ويغسل يسراه وإن زاد على قدر الضرورة فأدخل الكف صار الماء مستعملاً قوله: (فإنه لا يدري أين باتت يده أي أوت يده فلا يختص بنوم الليل، وجعله الإمام أحمد قاصراً على نوم الليل دون نوم النهار . قوله : ( وإذا لم يمكن إمالة الإناء) كيفية الغسل على ما ذكره أصحاب المذهب إنه إذا كان الإناء صغيراً يمكن رفعه لا يدخل يده فيه، بل يرفعه بشماله، ويصب على كفه اليمنى، فيغسلها ثلاثاً، ثم يأخذ الإناء بيمينه ويصب على كفه اليسرى فيغسلها ثلاثاً وإن كان الإناء كبيراً بحيث لا تمكن إمالته ، فإن كان معه إناء صغير رفع من الماء بذلك الإناء، وغسل يديه كما بينا، وإن لم يكن معه إناء صغير يدخل أصابع يده اليسرى مضمومة دون الكف ويرفع الماء، ويصب على كفه اليمنى، ويدلك الأصابع بعضها ببعض، يفعل ذلك ثلاثاً، ثم يدخل يده اليمني في الإناء بالغاً ما بلغ إن شاء الله، ويفعل باليسرى كذلك اهـ. قوله: (صار الماء مستعملاً) مخالف لما في الخانية، ونصها المحدث، أو الجنب إذا أدخل يده في الماء للاعتراف، وليس عليها نجاسة لا يفسد الماء، وكذا إذا وقع الكوز في الجب، وأدخل يده إلى المرفق لا . يصير الماء مستعملاً اهـ وتقييده في الخانية بالاعتراف أي بنيته يفيد أنه إذا نوى الغسل الماء مستعملاً ويه صرح في الدر حيث قال : فلو أدخل الكف إن أراد الغسل صار الماء مستعملاً، وإن أراد الإعتراف لا اهـ واعلم أن المحكوم عليه بالاستعمال عند إرادة الغسل هو الملاقي ليده لا كل الماء ذكره السيد ومعنى الإغتراف: نقل الماء من نحو الإناء، ثم إذا صار في یده نوی به التطهير
Tilting the vessel: he inserts the fingers of his left hand free from confirmed impurity and pours on his right palm until it is clean, then he inserts the right and washes the left. And if he exceeds the necessary amount by inserting the palm, the water becomes used. His statement: 'For he does not know where his hand spent the night' means his hand [spent the night], so it is not specific to night sleep, and Imam Ahmad restricted it to night sleep not day sleep. His statement: 'And if tilting the vessel is not possible' – the method of washing as mentioned by the companions of the madhhab: if the vessel is small and can be lifted, he does not insert his hand into it, but lifts it with his left and pours on his right palm, washing it three times, then takes the vessel with his right and pours on his left palm, washing it three times. If the vessel is large such that tilting is not possible, then if he has a small vessel he lifts water with that vessel and washes his hands as we explained; if he has no small vessel, he inserts the fingers of his left hand held together without the palm and lifts water, pours on his right palm, and rubs the fingers against each other, doing that three times, then inserts his right hand into the vessel as far as it reaches, God willing, and does likewise with the left. End. His statement: 'the water becomes used' contradicts what is in al-Khaniyyah, whose text: the hadath or junub if he inserts his hand into water for scooping, and there is no impurity on it, does not spoil the water; likewise if the jug falls into the well and he inserts his hand up to the elbow, the water does not become used. End. And his restriction in al-Khaniyyah to 'scooping' i.e. by his intention indicates that if he intends washing, the water becomes used. This is explicitly stated in al-Durr where he said: 'If he inserts the palm intending washing, the water becomes used; if intending scooping, it does not.' End. Know that the water ruled as used when intending washing is the water that contacts his hand, not all the water – as mentioned by al-Sayyid. The meaning of scooping (ightiraf) is transferring water from something like a vessel; then when it is in his hand he intends purification with it.
Source pages p. 66

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the Hashiya on the Maraqi al-Falah. It discusses the sunnah of washing hands upon waking from sleep by tilting a vessel of water, and the fiqh of used water (musta'mal). The matn states that one should insert only the fingers of the left hand (free from confirmed impurity) into the water and pour on the right palm, then wash the left hand with the right. If one exceeds the necessary amount by inserting the whole palm, the water becomes musta'mal (used) and cannot be used for purification. The hashya then expands on the proof: the hadith 'he does not know where his hand spent the night' is cited as the reason for this washing, and Imam Ahmad is noted to restrict it to night sleep only. Then detailed methods are given for when the vessel cannot be tilted: for a small vessel, lift and pour; for a large vessel without a small vessel, insert only the fingers without the palm, lift water, and wash three times. The hashya then addresses a seeming contradiction: in al-Khaniyyah it says water does not become musta'mal if one inserts the hand for scooping (ightiraf) without impurity. The author resolves this by noting that intention matters: if one intends washing (ghusl), the water becomes musta'mal; if intending only to scoop water for later purification, it does not. This is the relied-upon position (mu'tamad) as in al-Durr. Additionally, only the water that contacts the hand becomes musta'mal, not the entire body of water. The term 'ightiraf' is defined as transferring water from a vessel. This passage guards against misunderstanding that any insertion of hand renders water musta'mal.

Key Terms
ماء مستعمل (ma' musta'mal): Water that has been used for purification and is no longer suitable for the same purpose.
إغتراف (ightiraf): Scooping water from a vessel with the hand without intending immediate purification.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person wakes up from sleep and inserts his entire palm into a vessel of water with the intention of just scooping water to pour into another container, does the water become musta'mal according to the relied-upon Hanafi position?
A) Yes, because any insertion of the hand makes water musta'mal.
B) No, because he intended to scoop, not to wash.
C) Yes, because he is in a state of hadath.
D) No, only if the water contacts an impurity.

Key Takeaway
Intention determines whether water becomes musta'mal: washing renders it used, scooping does not.

Basmalah at the Start of Wudu: Sunnah Mu'akkadah
Ruling on basmalah as a sunnah and intra-Hanafi debate

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on basmalah at the start of wudu, identify the proof and its interpretation, and explain the difference between wudu and eating regarding making up the sunnah.

Core Idea
Basmalah at wudu's start is sunnah mu'akkadah — if forgotten, saying it later does not recover the sunnah for the beginning.

The basmalah (saying 'Bismillah') at the beginning of wudu is a well-established practice in the Hanafi school. The matn of Maraqi al-Falah lists it as a sunnah. But what does that mean exactly? Is it obligatory, recommended, or something in between? And what if you forget? This lesson unpacks the details from the Hashiya, showing how Hanafi authorities weigh the evidence and reach the relied-upon ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is saying 'Bismillah' at the beginning of wudu. The ruling under discussion: is it sunnah mu'akkadah, mustahabb, or wajib?
The matn implies sunnah, but the Hashiya clarifies the strength.
2
Examine the primary dalil
The hadith 'La wudu' liman lam yadhkur ism Allah' (Abu Dawud, Tirmidhi, Hakim) is cited. Understand its wording and chain.
The hadith is ahad (zanni thubut) and its meaning (dalalah) is also zanni.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
The negation 'la wudu' is interpreted as negation of perfection (nafy al-kamal), not absolute validity. Hence, the ruling is sunnah, not fard or wajib.
This interpretive principle is key to understanding how Hanafis derive rulings.
4
Trace the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Al-Hidayah considered it mustahabb due to perceived weakness; al-Kamal argued for wujub by analogy with Fatiha. The majority (including the author of the Hashiya) favor sunnah mu'akkadah due to the hadith's authentication and multiple chains.
The tarjih relies on the strength of the hadith as hasan.
5
Apply the ruling to a scenario of forgetting
If one forgets basmalah at the start and remembers during wudu, the sunnah for the beginning is not attained. However, one should still say it to avoid an empty wudu (mandub). This contrasts with eating, where saying basmalah during the meal covers the past and future.
The distinction shows the precision of Hanafi fiqh in applying sunnah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (والتسمية ابتداء) عدها من السنن المؤكدة هو ما في المبسوط، ومحيط رضى الدين والتحفة وغيرها واختاره القدوري والطحاوي وصاحب الكافي وصححه المرغيناني لقوله : لا صلاة لمن لا ضوء له ولا وضوء لمن لم يذكر اسم الله عليه رواه أبو داود والترمذي والحاكم، وهو محمول على نفي الكمال، وقال في الهداية : الأصح أنها مستحبة وكأن وجهه ضعف الحديث والأظهر أنه لا ينزل عن درجة الحسن لاعتضاده بكثرة الطرق والشواهد فكان حجة حتى أن الكمال أثبت به الوجوب، كما أن . وجوب الفاتحة ثبت بمثله، وأما تعيين كونها في الإبتداء. فدليله ما روى عن عائشة كان رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم إذا مس طهوره الله تعالى ثم يفرغ الماء على بدنه قوله : (لا تحصل له السنة) وفي السراج أنه يأتي بها لئلا يخلو وضؤه عنها، ومثله في الجوهرة أي ليكون آتيا بالمندوب، وإن فاتته السنة كما في الدر، وقالوا : إنّها عند غسل كل عضو مندوبة ذكره السيد قوله : (بخلاف الأكل) فإنه إذا أتى بها أثناءه تحصل السنة في الماضي والباقي كما ذكره الحلبي متعقباً الكمال في قوله : إنما تحصل السنة في الباقي فقط. قوله : لقوله صلى الله عليه وسلم الخ) الأولى في الاستدلال ما ذكره آنفاً. سمي اسم الله فإنه يظهر جسده كله ومن توضأ ولم يذكر اسم الله لم يطهر إلا موضع الوضوء، والمنقول عن السلف، وقيل عن النبي في لفظها باسم الله العظيم والحمد لله على دين الإسلام وقيل الأفضل بسم الله الرحمن الرحيم لعموم كل أمر ذي بال الحديث، ويسمي كذلك قبل الاستنجاء وكشف العورة في الأصح ( والسواك) بكسر السين اسم للاستياك وللعود أيضاً والمراد الأول لقوله : لولا أن أشق على أمتي لأمرتهم بالسواك عند كل صلاة، أو مع كل صلاة)، ولما ورد أن كل صلاة به تفضل سبعين صلاة بدونه وينبغي يكون لينا في غلظ الأصبع طول شبر مستوياً قليل العقد من الأراك وهو من سنن الوضوء ووقته المسنون في ابتدائه لأنّ الابتداء به سنة أيضاً عند المضمضة على قول الأكثر وقال أن قوله: (فإنه يظهر جسده كله الخ) لعل الثمرة تظهر في كثرة الثواب، وقلته ولفظ هذا الحديث لا يعين البسملة، ولذا قال في المحيط : لو قال نحو لا إله إلا الله مقيماً للسنة . يصير قال ابن أمير حاج ويؤيده حديث كل أمر لا يبدأ فيه بذكر الله اهـ، فلو كبر، أو هلل، أو حمد كان مقيماً للسنة أي لأصلها وكمالها لما سبق ذكره السيد قوله : (باسم الله العظيم الخ) أي بعد إتيانه بالتعوذ قاله الوبري. قوله : (والحمد الله على دين الإسلام) الذي في الخبازية والحمد لله على الإسلام. قوله : (وقيل الأفضل الخ) في البناية عن المجتبى، لو قال: بسم الله الرحمن الرحيم باسم الله العظيم والحمد لله على الإسلام فحسن لورود الآثار اهـ أي بعد التعوذ. قوله: (ويسمي كذلك قبل الاستنجاء) أي بالصيغة المتقدمة على الخلاف، والذي سبق أنه كان إذا دخل الخلاء قال : «باسم الله اللهم إني أعوذ بك من الخبث والخبائث) اهـ، قبل الاستنجاء لأنه ملحق بالوضوء من حيث أنه طهارة وظاهر هذا أنه قاصر على الاستنجاء بالماء وبه قيد الزيلعي والإطلاق أولى كما لا يخفى ذكره بعض الأفاضل، وعلة وإنما يسمي التسمية بعده عند الوضوء إنّه ابتداء الطهارة ذكره السيد
His statement: 'And the basmalah at the beginning' – counting it among the confirmed sunnah is what is in al-Mabsut, Muhit Radhi al-Din, al-Tuhfah, and others; al-Quduri, al-Tahawi, the author of al-Kafi chose it, and al-Marghinani authenticated it due to his statement: 'There is no prayer for one who has no wudu, and no wudu for one who does not mention the name of Allah upon it' – narrated by Abu Dawud, al-Tirmidhi, and al-Hakim. It is interpreted as negation of perfection. Al-Hidayah said: the correct view is that it is mustahabb, as if its face is the weakness of the hadith. But the apparent view is that it does not fall below the degree of hasan because it is strengthened by many chains and witnesses, so it is a proof; even al-Kamal established obligation by it, just as the obligation of al-Fatiha was established by similar. As for specifying it at the beginning, its proof is what is narrated from Aisha: 'When the Messenger of Allah (ﷺ) touched his purification water, he would say 'Bismillah' then pour water over his body.' His statement: 'He does not attain the sunnah' – In al-Siraj: he should still do it so that his wudu is not empty of it; similar in al-Jawharah, i.e., he should perform the recommended (mandub) even if the sunnah is missed, as in al-Durr. They said: It is recommended at washing each limb, mentioned by al-Sayyid. His statement: 'contrary to eating' – because if he does it during eating, the sunnah is attained for the past and remaining, as mentioned by al-Halabi commenting on al-Kamal who said it is only attained for the remaining. His statement: 'For his saying (ﷺ)...' – the best evidence is what he mentioned earlier. 'He mentions the name of Allah, for it makes his entire body manifest, and whoever performs wudu without mentioning Allah's name, only the place of wudu is purified.' This is transmitted from the Salaf, and it is said from the Prophet in its wording: 'Bismillah al-Azim wal-hamdu lillahi ala din al-Islam.' And it is said the best is 'Bismillah al-Rahman al-Rahim' due to the generality of the hadith 'every matter of importance'. He also says it before istinja' and uncovering the private parts in the correct view. (And the siwak) – with kasrah of the sin, it is a noun for the act of using siwak and also for the stick; the first meaning is intended due to his saying: 'Were it not that I would burden my ummah, I would have ordered them with siwak at every prayer' or 'with every prayer'. And because it is narrated that every prayer with it is superior to seventy prayers without it. It should be soft, about the thickness of a finger, a span in length, straight, having few knots, from the arak tree. It is from the sunan of wudu, and its prescribed time is at its beginning because beginning with it is also sunnah at the time of rinsing the mouth according to the majority. And he said: 'His statement: 'For it makes his entire body manifest' – perhaps the benefit appears in abundance or scarcity of reward. The wording of this hadith does not specify the basmalah, so in al-Muhit: if he says something like 'La ilaha illa Allah' intending the sunnah, it suffices. Ibn Amir Haj said: the hadith 'Every matter not begun with the remembrance of Allah' supports this. So if he says takbir, tahlil, or tahmid, he fulfills the sunnah i.e. its essence and perfection as previously mentioned by al-Sayyid. His statement: 'Bismillah al-Azim etc.' i.e. after seeking refuge (ta'awwudh) as said by al-Wabri. His statement: 'wal-hamdu lillahi ala din al-Islam' – in al-Khabbazi: 'al-hamdu lillahi ala al-Islam.' His statement: 'And it is said the best etc.' – in al-Binayah from al-Mujtaba: if he says 'Bismillah al-Rahman al-Rahim, Bismillah al-Azim, wal-hamdu lillahi ala al-Islam' that is good due to reports. i.e. after ta'awwudh. His statement: 'And he says it similarly before istinja'' i.e. with the aforementioned formula according to the difference of opinion. What preceded is that when he entered the toilet he would say: 'Bismillah, Allahumma inni a'udhu bika min al-khubthi wa al-khaba'ith' before istinja' because it is attached to wudu in that it is purification. The apparent meaning is that it is restricted to istinja' with water; al-Zayla'i restricted it, but the unrestricted is better as is not hidden. Mentioned by some virtuous. The reason he says the tasmiyah after it in wudu is that it is the beginning of purification, mentioned by al-Sayyid.
Source pages p. 66

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the Hashiya concerning the basmalah (tasmiyah) at the beginning of wudu. The matn states that basmalah is a sunnah of wudu and it is specifically at the start. The hashya discusses its legal status: many Hanafi authorities (al-Mabsut, Muhit, al-Tuhfah, al-Quduri, al-Tahawi, al-Kafi, al-Marghinani) consider it a sunnah mu'akkadah, citing the hadith 'La wudu' liman lam yadhkur ism Allah'. Al-Hidayah says it is mustahabb due to the weakness of the hadith, but the author of the hashya argues the hadith is hasan due to multiple chains, making it a proof. Some even argued for obligation (wujub) like al-Kamal, but the relied-upon view is sunnah mu'akkadah. The proof for it being at the beginning is the hadith of Aisha that the Prophet would say basmalah before pouring water. If one forgets to say it at the beginning and remembers during the wudu, the sunnah is not attained for the completed parts; however, one should still say it to avoid an empty wudu. This differs from eating, where saying basmalah during the meal attains the sunnah for both past and future. The hashya also discusses the wording: the preferred is 'Bismillah al-Rahman al-Rahim' due to the hadith about every important matter, though other formulations like 'Bismillah al-Azim' are also reported. Basmalah is also said before istinja' and uncovering the private parts. This passage guards against a common misunderstanding: that if one forgets basmalah at the start, saying it later does not make up for the sunnah of the beginning, unlike eating where it does.

Key Terms
التسمية (al-tasmiyah): Uttering 'Bismillah' at the beginning of wudu.
السنة المؤكدة (al-sunnah al-mu'akkadah): A confirmed, consistently practiced sunnah; omitting it is disliked but not sinful.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position, what is the ruling on saying basmalah at the beginning of wudu?
A) Fard (obligatory)
B) Wajib (necessary)
C) Sunnah mu'akkadah (confirmed sunnah)
D) Mustahabb (recommended)

Key Takeaway
The basmalah at the start of wudu is sunnah mu'akkadah; if forgotten, saying it later does not recover the sunnah but is still recommended.

Siwak as a Sunnah of Wudu: Ruling and Evidence
Ruling with proof for siwak as sunnah of wudu

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on siwak in wudu, identify the supporting dalil, and distinguish between the Hanafi and Shafi'i positions on its timing.

Core Idea
Siwak is a sunnah mu'akkadah of wudu, not of prayer – its virtue attaches to purification.

In this passage, the author confirms that siwak is a sunnah of wudu performed at the beginning, specifically when rinsing the mouth. The hashya provides key evidence from the Sunnah and clarifies a common inter-madhhab dispute about the timing. Understanding this ruling will help you correctly practice and teach the sunnah of siwak.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The text states that siwak is from the sunan of wudu. Determine the hukm level: sunnah mu'akkadah. Note the time: at the beginning, during mouth rinsing.
The ruling is not wajib or fard; it is a confirmed sunnah.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites the hadith 'Lawla an ashuqqa 'ala ummati la-amartuhum bi al-siwak' and emphasizes the version with 'at every wudu' from Nasa'i.
The version 'at every prayer' would support Shafi'i, so the Hanafi rely on the wudu narration.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The phrase 'lawla' (were it not) indicates that the Prophet would have made it obligatory if not for hardship, thus it is a highly recommended sunnah (sunnah mu'akkadah).
This linguistic indicator shows the strength of the recommendation, even though the thubut is zanni.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
The Shafi'i school holds that siwak is sunnah at every prayer, based on the 'at every prayer' narration. The Hanafi school holds it is sunnah at every wudu.
The hashya explicitly critiques the author for citing the prayer version and prefers the wudu version.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi position is supported by the Nasa'i narration, authenticated by Hakim, and cited by Bukhari as a ta'liq. Thus, the sunnah is attached to wudu, and its virtue applies to all prayers performed with that wudu.
This explains why one need not repeat siwak for each prayer if the wudu is still valid.

(And the siwak) – with kasrah of the sin, it is a noun for the act of using siwak and also for the stick; the first meaning is intended due to his saying: 'Were it not that I would burden my ummah, I would have ordered them with siwak at every prayer' or 'with every prayer'. And because it is narrated that every prayer with it is superior to seventy prayers without it. The reason he says the tasmiyah after it in wudu is that it is the beginning of purification, mentioned by al-Sayyid. His statement: 'and the first meaning is intended' i.e. no need to estimate a construct phrase. His statement: 'I would have ordered them with siwak at every prayer' – this does not support our madhhab, but rather the madhhab of al-Shafi'i; what supports our madhhab is the narration of al-Nasa'i 'at every wudu' which al-Hakim authenticated and al-Bukhari mentioned as a ta'liq in the Book of Fasting. So if the author had restricted to that, it would have been better. His statement: 'and because it is narrated that every prayer with it...' – this virtue is attained in every prayer performed with a wudu in which one used siwak, even if he did not use siwak at the time of standing for prayer, because it is from the sunan of the religion not from the sunan of the prayer according to the correct view as we will mention if Allah wills. His statement: 'and it should be soft etc.' – some have the expression: it is recommended that even if it is dry, he should wet it and wash it after use lest the devil use it; it should be from a bitter tree to cut phlegm, and be purer for the chest, and more beneficial for food, and the best is arak, then olive; and it is valid with any stick except pomegranate and sugarcane due to their harm; it should be a span in length because if longer the devil mounts on it. End. His statement: 'because beginning with it is also sunnah at the time of rinsing the mouth' – to complete cleanliness; this is the choice of Shaykh al-Islam in...

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof concerning siwak as a sunnah of wudu. The matn states that siwak is a sunnah, performed at the beginning of wudu alongside rinsing the mouth. The hashya provides evidence: the hadith 'Lawla an ashuqqa 'ala ummati la-amartuhum bi al-siwak 'inda kulli salah' and the narration that each prayer with siwak is superior to seventy without. The preferred siwak is soft, finger-thick, a span long, straight, with few knots, from the arak tree. The hashya also addresses the basmalah discussion tangentially, explaining that if one fails to say the exact basmalah but says 'La ilaha illa Allah' with the intention of sunnah, it suffices. Then a key point: the hadith 'inda kulli salah' supports the Shafi'i position; the Hanafi position is supported by the narration 'inda kulli wudu' from Nasa'i. The virtue of siwak is attached to the wudu, not the prayer itself, so if one performs wudu with siwak, the virtue applies to all prayers performed with that wudu even if siwak is not repeated. The hashya also discusses the recommended properties of the siwak stick and the ruling that it is valid from any wood except pomegranate and sugarcane due to harm. The passage guards against misunderstanding that siwak is a sunnah of prayer itself; rather, it is a sunnah of wudu and thus its virtue is tied to the state of purification.

Key Terms
السواك (al-siwak): The act of cleaning the teeth with a stick; also the stick itself. Here it is intended as the act.
الاستياك (al-istiyak): The verbal noun of using the siwak.

Key Takeaway
Siwak is a confirmed sunnah of wudu, and its practice is best at the start of wudu with the mouth rinse.

Ruling of Tasmiah in Wudu
Explains the ruling and wording of tasmiah in wudu

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on tasmiah in wudu and explain why it is sunnah rather than wajib.

Core Idea
Tasmiah is a sunnah muakkadah; omitting it does not invalidate wudu but reduces reward.

In this lesson, we examine the ruling on mentioning Allah's name (tasmiah) at the start of wudu. The Hanafi school considers it a strongly recommended sunnah, not an obligation, based on hadith evidence. We will explore the proof, the differing wordings, and how this applies to related acts like istinja.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is tasmiah (saying Bismillah) at the beginning of wudu. According to the Hanafi school, it is a sunnah muakkadah (emphatically recommended), not wajib.
2
Locate the dalil
The primary evidence is the hadith: 'Every important matter that does not begin with the remembrance of Allah is severed (from blessing).' This is cited in the hashya.
The hadith is narrated by Abu Dawud and others.
3
Analyze the dalil's implication
In Hanafi usul, a general command (amr) indicates recommendation (nadb) unless there is a contextual clue (qarinah) that makes it obligatory. The hadith uses 'remembrance of Allah' which can be fulfilled by any dhikr, not specifically basmalah, and does not demand repetition if omitted.
4
Note the critical refinement
The hashya clarifies that the hadith does not specify basmalah; any dhikr (e.g., takbir, tahlil, hamd) suffices for the sunnah. The best is the complete basmalah.
5
Apply to related acts
Tasmiah is also recommended before istinja and before uncovering the private parts, as it is a purification act similar to wudu.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اسم الله فإنه يظهر جسده كله ومن توضأ ولم يذكر اسم الله لم يطهر إلا موضع الوضوء، والمنقول عن السلف، وقيل عن النبي في لفظها باسم الله العظيم والحمد لله على دين الإسلام وقيل الأفضل بسم الله الرحمن الرحيم لعموم كل أمر ذي بال الحديث، ويسمي كذلك قبل الاستنجاء وكشف العورة في الأصح (قوله: (فإنه يظهر جسده كله الخ) لعل الثمرة تظهر في كثرة الثواب، وقلته ولفظ هذا الحديث لا يعين البسملة، ولذا قال في المحيط : لو قال نحو لا إله إلا الله مقيماً للسنة . يصير قال ابن أمير حاج ويؤيده حديث كل أمر لا يبدأ فيه بذكر الله اهـ، فلو كبر، أو هلل، أو حمد كان مقيماً للسنة أي لأصلها وكمالها لما سبق ذكره السيد قوله : (باسم الله العظيم الخ) أي بعد إتيانه بالتعوذ قاله الوبري. قوله : (والحمد الله على دين الإسلام) الذي في الخبازية والحمد لله على الإسلام. قوله : (وقيل الأفضل الخ) في البناية عن المجتبى، لو قال: بسم الله الرحمن الرحيم باسم الله العظيم والحمد لله على الإسلام فحسن لورود الآثار اهـ أي بعد التعوذ. قوله: (ويسمي كذلك قبل الاستنجاء) أي بالصيغة المتقدمة على الخلاف، والذي سبق أنه كان إذا دخل الخلاء قال : «باسم الله اللهم إني أعوذ بك من الخبث والخبائث) اهـ، قبل الاستنجاء لأنه ملحق بالوضوء من حيث أنه طهارة وظاهر هذا أنه قاصر على الاستنجاء بالماء وبه قيد الزيلعي والإطلاق أولى كما لا يخفى ذكره بعض الأفاضل، وعلة التسمية بعده عند الوضوء إنّه ابتداء الطهارة ذكره السيد
Saying the name of Allah, indeed it purifies his entire body. And whoever performs wudu and does not mention the name of Allah, only the place of wudu is purified. And what is transmitted from the Salaf, and it is said from the Prophet in its wording: 'With the name of Allah, the Mighty, and praise be to Allah for the religion of Islam' and it is said the best is 'Bismillah al-Rahman al-Rahim' due to the generality of every important matter (the hadith). And he says it similarly before istinja and uncovering the private parts according to the correct view. (His saying: 'Indeed it purifies his entire body etc.') Perhaps the benefit appears in abundance of reward and its lack. The wording of this hadith does not specify the basmala. Hence it is said in al-Muhit: If he says something like 'La ilaha illa Allah' intending the sunnah, it suffices. Ibn Amir Haj said, and it is supported by the hadith: 'Every important matter that does not begin with the remembrance of Allah' etc. So if he said takbir, tahlil, or tahmid, he fulfills the sunnah, i.e., its basis and perfection, as mentioned by al-Sayyid. His saying: 'With the name of Allah, the Mighty etc.' means after seeking refuge (ta'awwudh), as stated by al-Webri. His saying: 'And praise be to Allah for the religion of Islam' which is in al-Khazzaziyyah: 'And praise be to Allah for Islam.' His saying: 'And it is said the best etc.' In al-Binayah from al-Mujtaba: If he says 'Bismillah al-Rahman al-Rahim, with the name of Allah, the Mighty, and praise be to Allah for Islam', it is good due to the transmitted reports etc., i.e., after seeking refuge. His saying: 'And he says it similarly before istinja' means with the aforementioned formula according to the difference of opinion. What has preceded is that when he entered the toilet he said: 'Bismillah, O Allah I seek refuge in You from male and female devils' etc., before istinja because it is attached to wudu in that it is purification. The apparent meaning is that it is limited to istinja with water, and al-Zayla'i restricted it thus, but the general application is more appropriate as some nobles mentioned. And the reason for saying it after wudu is that it is the beginning of purification, as mentioned by al-Sayyid.
Source pages p. 67

Commentary
This is a passage from the Hashiya of al-Tahtawi explaining the ruling on mentioning Allah's name (tasmiah) in wudu. The base text (Maraqi al-Falah) states that tasmiah purifies the entire body, and if one omits it, only the limbs washed are purified. The commentator clarifies that the reward varies, and the hadith does not mandate a specific wording. Any remembrance of Allah (e.g., 'La ilaha illa Allah') suffices for the sunnah, though the best is the complete formula including 'Bismillah al-Rahman al-Rahim'. The hashya also discusses saying tasmiah before istinja (cleansing after answering the call of nature) and before uncovering the private parts, agreeing that it is recommended. The ruling is that tasmiah is a sunnah (recommended) act, not obligatory, and its omission does not invalidate wudu.

Key Terms
التسمية (al-tasmiah): Mentioning the name of Allah (e.g., Bismillah) at the start of an act.
الاستنجاء (al-istinja): Cleansing the private parts with water or stones after using the toilet.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on saying Bismillah at the beginning of wudu according to the Hanafi school?
A) It is fard (obligatory); omission invalidates wudu.
B) It is sunnah; omission does not invalidate wudu but loses reward.
C) It is mustahab but not sunnah.
D) It is makruh to say it.

Key Takeaway
Tasmiah is a sunnah muakkadah in wudu; omitting it does not invalidate the wudu.

Rulings on Siwak and Its Virtues
Ruling on siwak with proof, occasions, method, and virtues

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on siwak, explain its legal classification and the recommended occasions, and identify the correct method of use.

Core Idea
Siwak is a sunnah muakkadah with broad recommendation; its virtue is attained even with simple substitutes, and it brings immense spiritual and worldly benefits.

Siwak is a confirmed practice of the Prophet ﷺ that goes beyond oral hygiene. The Hanafi school classifies it as a sunnah of the religion, recommended at many occasions. This lesson unpacks its ruling, the evidence, the proper method, and the remarkable virtues narrated by the scholars.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and evidence
State the hukm level (sunnah muakkadah) and cite the hadith 'السواك مطهرة للفم مرضاة للرب' as the primary dalil.
The hadith uses commendation, indicating recommendation (nadb), not obligation.
2
Note the intra-Hanafi dispute
Understand the difference of opinion on whether siwak is sunnah of wudu, salah, or the religion, and the preferred view that it is sunnah of the religion.
The preferred view is transmitted from Imam Abu Hanifa and affirmed by al-Hidayah and al-‘Ayni.
3
List the recommended occasions
Identify the occasions: change of mouth odor, waking from sleep, before salah, entering house, gatherings, reciting Quran and hadith.
These are derived from the general encouragement and specific reports.
4
Describe the proper method and substitutes
Learn the sunnah way of holding the siwak and the alternatives (finger, rough cloth, chewing gum for women) when siwak is unavailable.
The method is from the narration of Ibn Mas'ud; substitutes are allowed in absence.
5
Recognize the extensive virtues
Review the spiritual and worldly benefits listed in the passage, understanding that they encourage consistent practice.
Even if some reports are weak, the scholars advised acting upon them for hope of reward.

And washing the hands before wudu, and it is from the sunan of wudu according to us, not from the sunan of salah. So its virtue is attained for every salah performed with a wudu in which one used siwak. And it is recommended for change of mouth odor, rising from sleep, and before salah, entering the house, gathering of people, and reciting Quran and hadith, due to the saying of the Imam: it is from the sunan of the religion. And he (peace be upon him) said: Siwak is a purification for the mouth and a means of pleasing the Lord. So it is equal in all states. And its virtue is attained even if one uses the finger or a rough cloth in its absence, i.e., the siwak, or if one has lost his teeth or has harm to his mouth, due to his saying (peace be upon him): Fingers suffice for siwak. And Ali (may Allah be pleased with him) said: Rubbing with the forefinger and thumb is siwak. And chewing gum stands in its place for women due to the delicacy of their skin. And the sunnah in holding it is to place your little finger of the right hand below it, the ring and middle fingers above it, and the thumb below its tip, as narrated by Ibn Mas'ud (may Allah be pleased with him). And do not grasp it because it causes hemorrhoids, and it is disliked lying down because it causes pride. The knower of Allah, Shaykh Ahmad al-Zahid, collected its virtues in a work titled Tuhfat al-Sulak. And the commentary: his saying: (and before salah) the place of recommendation in that is when one is safe from blood coming out; otherwise no. His saying: the saying of the Imam that it is from the sunan of the religion: the scholars differed on whether it is from the sunan of wudu, or salah, or the religion; the third is strongest, and it is the transmitted from the Imam as mentioned by al-'Ayni in his commentary on Bukhari, and his saying in al-Hidayah: the most correct is that it is mustahabb, meaning in wudu, not absolutely. And al-Kamal explained it because nothing has come that indicates the Prophet's persistence upon it at wudu, then he said: the truth is that it is from the sunan of the religion. And it is not recommended for one whom constant use harms; rather he should do it occasionally as researched by Ibn Amir Haj. His saying: (and its virtue is attained etc.) meaning the promised reward is consequent upon it. His saying: (in its absence, not in its presence) as in al-Kafi. His saying: (fingers suffice for siwak) the 'min' is for substitution. His saying: (rubbing with the forefinger and thumb is siwak) al-tashwis is rubbing with the hand, mentioned in al-Qamus among meanings; its manner as in Ibn Amir Haj is to begin with the thumb from the right side, using it above and below, then with the forefinger from the left side similarly. His saying: (and chewing gum stands in its place for women) it is known that reward is not attained for them except with intention; then apparently they are not commanded to use gum at the beginning of wudu like siwak for men, and it needs verification. His saying: (and the sunnah in holding it is to place your little finger etc.) the scholar Nuh discussed this and said: what is understood from the ahadith is beginning from the right side; as for holding it in the right hand, no; so it should be in the left hand because it is from the category of removing filth. And in it: since it is established from Ibn Mas'ud, no discussion. And it is recommended to rub the teeth, their outer and inner parts and edges, and the palate which is the inner and upper part of the mouth from inside, and the lower part from the front of the jaws. And Bukhari narrated from Abu Musa al-Ash'ari: I came to the Prophet (peace be upon him) and found him using siwak, saying 'A' a'. And siwak in his saying: (and do not grasp it etc.) and do not suck it because it causes blindness, and it is disliked with something harmful, and forbidden with something poisonous, and one swallows clear saliva from blood as it is beneficial for leprosy, vitiligo, and every disease of death. The book of purification. Page 69. On the virtues of siwak. (And rinsing the mouth) and it is technically reaching water to the entire mouth, and linguistically movement. And it is sunnah to be three times because he (peace be upon him) never performed wudu without rinsing three times and snuffing three times, taking new water for each. (And if) one rinses three times (with one handful), he has fulfilled the sunnah of rinsing but not the sunnah of repetition. (And snuffing) which is linguistically from 'al-nashq' meaning drawing water and the like by the breath of the nose, and technically reaching water to the soft part of the nose (al-marin), and it is done with three handfuls due to the hadith, and three with one is not valid. Abbas and Ata (may Allah be pleased with them all) said: adhere to siwak, do not neglect it, and persist in it, for in it is the pleasure of the Most Merciful; and it multiplies the prayer to ninety-nine fold or four hundred fold; persistence in it brings spaciousness and wealth and ease of provision; it purifies the mouth, strengthens the gums, soothes headache and the veins of the head until no still vein beats nor does a pulling vein rest; it removes headache and phlegm, strengthens teeth, sharpens eyesight, corrects the stomach, strengthens the body, increases a man's eloquence, memory, and intelligence, purifies the heart, increases good deeds, pleases the angels, they shake hands with him for the light of his face, they escort him when he goes out to prayer, the bearers of the Throne seek forgiveness for him when he leaves the mosque, and the prophets and messengers seek forgiveness for him. Siwak is a cause of anger for Satan, drives him away, purifies the mind, aids digestion, increases offspring, passes over the Sirat like a flash of lightning, delays grey hair, gives the book in the right hand, strengthens the body for obedience to Allah, removes heat from the body, removes pain, strengthens the back, reminds of the testimony, eases the death pangs, whitens teeth, sweetens breath, clarifies character, sharpens the tongue, quickens understanding, cuts moisture, sharpens eyesight, multiplies reward, increases wealth and children, helps in fulfilling needs, expands the grave, comforts him in his grave, writes for him the reward of one who did not use siwak on that day, opens for him the doors of Paradise, the angels say: this one is following the prophets, treading in their footsteps, seeking their guidance every day; and closes for him the doors of Hell; he does not leave the world except as pure and purified; and the Angel of Death does not come to seize his soul except in the form in which he comes to the saints, and in some expressions the prophets; he does not leave the world until he is given a drink from the basin of our Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him), which is the sealed nectar. The highest of these is that it is a purification for the mouth and a means of pleasing the Lord. Some said: all these virtues are narrated, some marfu', some mawquf, and even if there is criticism in their chains, one should act upon them because of what has been reported: whoever hears of a reward from Allah and seeks it, Allah gives him that reward even if it is not so. End. And some of the mentioned things revert to some.
Source pages p. 68

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on the use of siwak (toothstick) in the Hanafi school. It begins by stating that washing the hands before wudu is from the sunan of wudu, not of salah, and that its virtue is attained for every salah performed with a wudu in which siwak was used. The text then lists the recommended occasions for siwak: change of mouth odor, upon waking from sleep, before going to salah, entering the house, social gatherings, and reciting Quran and hadith. This is based on the statement of Imam Abu Hanifa that siwak is from the sunan of the religion. The hadith of the Prophet (SAW) 'Siwak is a purification for the mouth and a means of pleasing the Lord' is cited, indicating that its virtue applies in all states. Even if one uses the finger or a rough cloth in the absence of a siwak, it suffices, as the Prophet said 'Fingers suffice for siwak' and Ali (RA) said 'Rubbing with the forefinger and thumb is siwak'. Chewing gum (al-‘alk) stands in place of siwak for women due to their delicate skin. The sunnah way of holding the siwak is described: place the little finger of the right hand below it, the ring and middle fingers above, and the thumb below the tip, as narrated by Ibn Mas'ud. Clenching it is disliked as it causes hemorrhoids, and using it lying down is disliked as it causes pride. The commentary then addresses various points: the recommended times are when one is safe from bleeding; the difference of opinion on whether siwak is from sunan al-wudu, al-salah, or al-din is resolved by preferring al-din, as transmitted from Imam Abu Hanifa and affirmed by al-‘Ayni and al-Hidayah; those who are harmed by frequent use should do it occasionally. The commentary also discusses that the virtue is attained in the absence of a siwak, not in its presence, and details the method of using the finger. The passage concludes with an extensive list of virtues of siwak, both spiritual and worldly, ranging from reward multiplication to health benefits, all of which support the strong recommendation to use it.

Key Terms
سواك (siwak): A piece of twig or root used for cleaning teeth; its use is a sunnah act.
استياك (istiyak): The act of using siwak.
تشويص (tashwis): Rubbing the teeth with the fingers in the absence of a siwak.
علك (‘alk): Chewing gum used as a substitute for siwak, especially for women.
خنصر (khinsir): Little finger, used in the sunnah way of holding the siwak.
إبهام (ibham): Thumb, placed below the tip of the siwak.

A) It is fard (obligatory) in wudu.
B) It is a sunnah of wudu or the religion.
C) It is a sunnah of salah only.
D) It is makruh (disliked).

Key Takeaway
Siwak is a sunnah muakkadah with broad recommendation; its virtue is attained even with simple substitutes, and it brings immense spiritual and worldly benefits.

Taharah — Purification
beginner
6 min
Madmadah and Istinshaq: Definitions and Sunnah Rulings
Definitions and sunnah rulings for madmadah and istinshaq

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the definitions of madmadah and istinshaq according to the Hanafi school, and apply the ruling that each is sunnah muakkadah performed three times with separate handfuls, distinguishing between the sunnah of the act and the sunnah of repetition.

Core Idea
Madmadah and istinshaq are sunnah muakkadah, each done thrice with fresh water.

This passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi defines two key acts in wudu: rinsing the mouth (madmadah) and snuffing water into the nose (istinshaq). Both are sunnah muakkadah, not fard. The text clarifies the proper method: three separate handfuls of water. Understanding these definitions and rulings is essential for correct wudu practice and appreciating the Hanafi position vis-à-vis other schools.

Guided Path
1
Define each term linguistically and technically
Identify the linguistic root (madmadah: movement; istinshaq: drawing by breath) and the technical fiqh definition (madmadah: reaching water to the entire mouth; istinshaq: reaching water to the soft part of the nose).
The technical definition is what governs the legal ruling.
2
State the ruling (hukm) for each
Both are sunnah muakkadah (emphasized sunnah) based on the Prophet's continuous practice. They are not fard or wajib in the Hanafi school.
Contrast with Shafi'i view where they are considered fard.
3
Detail the prescribed method: three times with separate water
The text says 'three times' and specifies that each time should be with a new handful (ghurfah). If one uses a single handful for three rinses, only the basic sunnah of the act is fulfilled, not the sunnah of repetition (tathlith).
The sunnah of repetition is satisfied only by using separate water for each rinse.
4
Distinguish between fulfilling the sunnah of the act vs. the sunnah of repetition
Performing the act (e.g., rinsing once) fulfills the sunnah of madmadah. Doing it three times with separate water fulfills the additional sunnah of tathlith. The text highlights this nuance.
This distinction is important for those seeking complete reward.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(والمضمضة) وهي اصطلاحاً استيعاب الماء جميع الفم، وفي اللغة التحريك، ويسن أن تكون (ثلاثاً) لأنه لا توضأ فمضمض ثلاثاً واستنشق ثلاثاً يأخذ لكل واحدة ماء جديداً (ولو) تمضمض ثلاثاً (بغرفة) واحدة أقام سنة المضمضة لا سنة التكرير (والاستنشاق) وهو لغة من النشق جذب الماء ونحوه بريح الأنف إليه واصطلاحاً إيصال الماء إلى المارن وهو ما لان من الأنف ويكون بثلاث غرفات للحديث ولا يصح التثليث بواحدة
(And rinsing the mouth) and it is technically reaching water to the entire mouth, and linguistically movement. And it is sunnah to be three times because he (peace be upon him) never performed wudu without rinsing three times and snuffing three times, taking new water for each. (And if) one rinses three times (with one handful), he has fulfilled the sunnah of rinsing but not the sunnah of repetition. (And snuffing) which is linguistically from 'al-nashq' meaning drawing water and the like by the breath of the nose, and technically reaching water to the soft part of the nose (al-marin), and it is done with three handfuls due to the hadith, and three with one is not valid.
Source pages p. 69

Commentary
This passage defines the two actions of madmadah (rinsing the mouth) and istinshaq (snuffing water into the nose) and states their rulings. Madmadah is technically reaching water to the entire mouth; linguistically it means movement. It is sunnah to perform it three times, each with fresh water, as the Prophet never performed wudu without doing so. If one rinses three times with a single handful (i.e., taking water once and rinsing three separate times from that handful), the sunnah of rinsing is fulfilled but the sunnah of repeating with fresh water is not. Istinshaq linguistically means drawing water into the nose by breath; technically it is reaching water to the soft part (al-marin). It too is done with three handfuls, each separate. Doing all three with one handful is not valid. The commentary (not fully shown) usually explains conditions and nuances.

Key Terms
مضمضة (madmadah): Rinsing the mouth by reaching water to all parts of the mouth.
استنشاق (istinshaq): Snuffing water into the nose up to the soft part (al-marin).
مارن (marin): The soft, fleshy part of the nose.
غرفة (ghurfah): A cupped handful of water.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person takes one handful of water and rinses his mouth three times with that same handful, which sunnah does he fulfill?
A) Sunnah of repetition (sunnat al-takrir).
B) Sunnah of rinsing (sunnat al-madmadah) but not repetition.
C) Both sunnahs are fulfilled.
D) Neither sunnah is fulfilled.

Key Takeaway
Madmadah and istinshaq are sunnah muakkadah to be done three times each with separate handfuls of water; using one handful only fulfills the basic sunnah, not the sunnah of repetition.

Madmadah and Istinshaq: Definitions and Rulings
Defines madmadah and istinshaq; lists virtues of siwak

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the definitions of madmadah and istinshaq, explain their ruling (sunnah) in the Hanafi school, and identify that each is performed three times with separate water.

Core Idea
Madmadah covers the entire mouth; istinshaq reaches the nose — both are sunnah, not fard.

In this lesson, we explore two important sunnah acts of wudu: madmadah (rinsing the mouth) and istinshaq (sniffing water into the nose). The source passage defines them precisely and clarifies the number of repetitions. Although often mistaken as obligatory, the Hanafi school classifies them as sunnah. We will also touch upon the extensive virtues of siwak mentioned in the same passage.

Guided Path
1
Define the terms
Identify the linguistic and terminological definitions of madmadah and istinshaq as provided in the text. Note that madmadah means to cover the entire mouth with water, and istinshaq means to reach water to the soft part of the nose.
2
Identify the ruling and number
From the text, determine the legal ruling (sunnah) and the recommended number of repetitions (three times each, with fresh water). Understand the difference between performing the act and the repetition.
The sunnah is established by hadith, making it part of the prophetic practice.
3
Appreciate the virtues of siwak
Review the long list of virtues for using siwak. While not all narrations are strong, the principle of seeking reward encourages their practice. Note the overarching benefit: 'a purifier for the mouth and a pleasure for the Lord.'
The virtues span worldly and spiritual benefits, including health, forgiveness, and ease in the grave.

Refining Conditions of Madmadah and Istinshaq
Hashiya commentary refining definitions and conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the non-conditions of madmadah and istinshaq and apply the ruling on tathlith with one handful of water.

Core Idea
Madmadah does not require intention or expectoration; istinshaq does not require breath-drawing; three rinses with one handful is invalid for istinshaq.

This lesson clarifies common misconceptions about the sunnah acts of rinsing the mouth (madmadah) and sniffing water (istinshaq) during wudu. The hashia of al-Tahtawi refines earlier definitions, distinguishing between linguistic and legal requirements, and highlights a key difference between madmadah and istinshaq regarding the performance of three rinses.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Acts and Their Legal Status
Recognize that madmadah and istinshaq are sunnah acts in wudu. The passage discusses their definitions and conditions.
2
Determine What is NOT a Condition
Note that intention (al-iradah) and expelling water (al-majj) are not conditions for madmadah. For istinshaq, drawing water with breath is not a condition legally, though it is linguistically.
This means the act is valid even if one does not intend or expel, and for istinshaq, simply letting water reach the nose suffices.
3
Understand the Ruling on Tathlith (Three Rinses) with One Handful
The passage states that performing three istinshaq rinses with one handful is not correct (invalid) because the nose does not trap water like the mouth does. For madmadah, it is permissible to do three rinses with one handful, though better with separate water.
The key reason: the nose cannot retain water, so each sniff requires fresh water to ensure coverage.
4
Apply the Ruling in Practice
When performing wudu, ensure that for istinshaq each sniff uses fresh water. For madmadah, one handful may suffice for three rinses, but the sunnah is to use fresh water each time.
This prevents common errors like using the same water for multiple sniffs.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (وهي اصطلاحاً (الخ) والإدارة، والمج ليسا بشرط، فلو شرب الماء عبا أجزأه ولو مصالاً كما في الفتح، لكن الأفضل أن يمجه لأنه ماء مستعمل كما في السراج قوله: (وهو لغة من النشق) محرك من باب تعب الشم. قوله: (واصطلاحاً الخ) أفاد أن الجذب بريح الأنف ليس شرطاً فيه شرعاً بخلافه لغة نهر قوله: (ولا يصح التثليث بواحدة) أي في الاستنشاق قالوا: ويكفيه أن يتمضمض، ثم يستنشق من كف واحدة لما بواحدة لعدم انطباق الأنف على باقي الماء بخلاف المضمضة
His saying: 'And it is terminologically etc.' and intention and expectoration are not conditions. If one drinks water by gulping, it suffices even if absorbed, as in al-Fath, but it is better to expel it because it is used water, as in al-Siraj. His saying: 'And it is linguistically from al-nashq' (with fatha) from the verb meaning to smell. His saying: 'And terminologically etc.' indicates that drawing with the breath is not a condition legally unlike linguistically. His saying: 'And doing three times with one handful is not correct' i.e. in istinshaq. They said: It suffices him to rinse his mouth, then sniff from one handful because the nose does not close over the remaining water unlike the mouth.
Source pages p. 69

Commentary
This hashiya commentary elaborates on the earlier definitions. It clarifies that for madmadah, it is not required to intend or to expel the water; simply swallowing it suffices, though expelling is better as the water becomes used. For istinshaq, the essential point is reaching water to the nose, not necessarily drawing it with breath. The commentator also explains the ruling on performing three rinses with one handful: for istinshaq it is not valid because the nose does not trap water like the mouth does, so each rinse must be with fresh water. This is based on the hadith practice.

Key Terms
المج (al-majj): Expelling water from the mouth after rinsing.
الاستنشاق (al-istinshaq): Sniffing water into the nose as part of wudu.
المضمضة (al-madmadah): Rinsing the mouth as part of wudu.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Valid
B) Invalid
C) Makruh
D) Wajib

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi wudu, intention and expectoration are not conditions for madmadah; drawing with breath is not required for istinshaq; and three rinses with one handful is invalid for istinshaq but permissible for madmadah.
