The Sunnah of Exaggeration in Rinsing and Sniffing
Ruling on mubalaghah for non-fasting person with proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling of mubalaghah in madmadah and istinshaq for non-fasting persons and explain the Hanafi position based on the hadith.

Core Idea
Exaggeration in rinsing and sniffing is sunnah for the non-fasting person, established by a clear command from the Prophet.

In wudu and ghusl, rinsing the mouth and sniffing water into the nose are sunnan. But what about exaggerating in them? The Hanafi school explains that it is encouraged to reach water to the extreme permissible limit, except when fasting. This lesson establishes the general ruling and its proof.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is mubalaghah (exaggeration) in madmadah and istinshaq. The ruling for non-fasting persons is sunnah – recommended but not obligatory.
The passage begins with 'ويسن المبالغة' (and it is sunnah to exaggerate).
2
Locate the dalil
The hadith quoted: 'بالغ في ضمضمة والاستنشاق إلا أن تكون صائماً' (exaggerate in rinsing and sniffing unless you are fasting).
This hadith is the primary evidence for the ruling.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
The imperative 'بالغ' indicates recommendation (nadb) in Hanafi usul, not obligation. The exception 'إلا أن تكون صائماً' shows that the ruling changes for the fasting person.
The imperative is interpreted as nadb because no qarinah indicates wujub.
4
Note the intra-madhhab ikhtilaf
Some Hanafi scholars considered mubalaghah wajib in ghusl. The mu'tamad (reliable view) is sunnah in both wudu and ghusl, as stated 'على المعتمد'.
The passage explicitly settles the ikhtilaf by stating the mu'tamad.
5
Understand the wisdom
Madmadah and istinshaq are placed before the fard acts in wudu to test the water's qualities (color, taste, smell) for purity, as explained by the commentator.
This wisdom shows the holistic nature of wudu beyond mere purification.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
و) يسن (المبالغة في المضمضة) وهو إيصال الماء لرأس الحلق (و) المبالغة في (الاستنشاق) وهي إيصاله إلى ما فوق المارن (لغير الصائم والصائم لا يبالغ فيهما خشية إفساد الصوم لقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام: (بالغ) في ضمضمة، والاستنشاق إلا أن تكون صائماً» والمبالغة فيهما هي سنة في الطهارتين على المعتمد، وقيل: سنة في. الوضوء واجبة في الغسل إلا أن يكون صائماً نقله القهستاني عن المنية وشارح الشرعة عن صلاة البقالي واعلم أن المضمضة والإستنشاق سنتان مشتملتان على سبع سنن الترتيب والتثليث والتجديد، وفعلهما باليمين، والمبالغة فيهما، والمج والاستنثار والحكمة في تقديمهما على الفروض إختبار أوصاف الماء لأن لونه يدرك بالبصر، وطعمه بالفم، وريحه بالأنف، فقدما لاختبار حال الماء بعد الرؤية قبل فعل الفرض به وقدمت المضمضة لشرف منافع الفم كما في ابن أمير حاج. قوله : (وهي إيصال الماء لرأس الحلق الخ) هو ما في الخلاصة، وقال الإمام خواهر زاده: هو في المضمضة الغرغرة وهي تردد الماء في الحلق وفي الإستنشاق أن يجذب الماء بنفسه إلى ما اشتد اهـ. قال في البحر وهو الأولى والاستنثار مطلوب، والإجماع على عدم وجوبه، والمستحب أن يستثر بيده اليسرى ويكره بغير يد لأنه يشبه فعل الدابة، وقيل لا يكره ذكره البدر العيني، والأولى أن يدخل اصبعه في فمه، وأنفه قهستاني قوله: (والصائم لا يبالغ) أي مطلقاً ولو صام نفل قوله : ( خشية إفساد الصوم) فهو مكروه كذوق شيء، ومضغه.
And it is sunnah to exaggerate in madmadah, which is reaching water to the top of the throat, and to exaggerate in istinshaq, which is reaching it above the soft part of the nose, for the non-fasting person. But the fasting person should not exaggerate in them for fear of spoiling the fast, due to his saying (peace be upon him): 'Exaggerate in rinsing and sniffing unless you are fasting.' And exaggeration in them is sunnah in both purifications according to the reliable view... (commentary) ... His saying: 'and the fasting person should not exaggerate' means absolutely, even if fasting a nafil fast. His saying: 'for fear of spoiling the fast' so it is makruh like tasting something and chewing it.
Source pages p. 70

Commentary
This passage discusses the ruling of mubalaghah (exaggeration) in madmadah and istinshaq. It is sunnah to reach water to the back of the throat in rinsing and above the soft part of the nose in sniffing for non-fasting persons. However, the fasting person is prohibited from doing so because it may invalidate the fast, based on a clear hadith. The commentary further explains that exaggeration is sunnah in both wudu and ghusl according to the relied-upon view, but some say it is wajib in ghusl. The wisdom of placing these actions before the fard acts is to test the qualities of water (color, taste, smell) before using it. The commentator also notes that istinshar (blowing the nose) is recommended but not obligatory, and it is sunnah to use the left hand for that. For a fasting person, any exaggeration is makruh because of the risk of breaking the fast.

Key Terms
المبالغة (al-mubalaghah): Exaggeration, i.e., reaching water to the extreme permitted limit in rinsing and sniffing.
المضمضة (al-madmadah): Rinsing the mouth with water.
الاستنشاق (al-istinshaq): Sniffing water into the nose.
الاستنثار (al-istinshar): Blowing the nose after istinshaq.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Wajib
B) Sunnah
C) Mubah
D) Makruh

Key Takeaway
Mubalaghah in madmadah and istinshaq is a sunnah act for non-fasting persons, established by the Prophet's command and confirmed as the mu'tamad in both wudu and ghusl.

5 min
Why the Fasting Person Avoids Exaggeration
Exception ruling for fasting person with commentary

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why mubalaghah is prohibited for the fasting person and identify the ruling (makruh) based on the hadith's exception.

Core Idea
For the fasting person, exaggerating in rinsing and sniffing is makruh because it risks breaking the fast.

The same hadith that encourages mubalaghah for non-fasting persons contains an explicit exception: 'إلا أن تكون صائماً' (unless you are fasting). This lesson explores the ruling for the fasting person, the reasoning (fear of spoiling the fast), and practical considerations like using the left hand for istinshar.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling for fasting
The passage states: 'والصائم لا يبالغ' (the fasting person should not exaggerate). The ruling is makruh, as clarified in the commentary: 'فهو مكروه'.
Makruh here is tanzihi (disliked, not sinful).
2
Understand the reason
The reason is 'خشية إفساد الصوم' (fear of spoiling the fast). If water reaches the throat and is swallowed, the fast breaks, so exaggeration is avoided as a precaution.
The word 'خشية' indicates a strong likelihood, not certainty.
3
Note the absolute application
The prohibition applies 'مطلقاً' (absolutely), even for nafl (voluntary) fasts, as the commentary says 'ولو صام نفل'.
This shows the ruling is comprehensive for all fasts.
4
Distinguish from similar actions
The passage compares mubalaghah to tasting and chewing food or drink, both of which are makruh for the fasting person for the same reason.
These actions are not haram unless something enters the throat.
5
Learn the recommended alternative
For istinshar (blowing the nose), it is recommended to use the left hand. Using something else is disliked (makruh) because it resembles an animal's action.
This is a separate sunnah related to the practice of istinshaq.

This passage discusses the ruling of mubalaghah (exaggeration) in madmadah and istinshaq. It is sunnah to reach water to the back of the throat in rinsing and above the soft part of the nose in sniffing for non-fasting persons. However, the fasting person is prohibited from doing so because it may invalidate the fast, based on a clear hadith. The commentary further explains that exaggeration is sunnah in both wudu and ghusl according to the relied-upon view, but some say it is wajib in ghusl. The wisdom of placing these actions before the fard acts is to test the qualities of water (color, taste, smell) before using it. The commentator also notes that istinshar (blowing the nose) is recommended but not obligatory, and it is sunnah to use the left hand for that. For a fasting person, any exaggeration is makruh because of the risk of breaking the fast.

Key Terms
صائم (sa'im): A person who is fasting.
خشية (khashyah): Fear, concern that something may happen.
الاستنثار (al-istinshar): Blowing the nose after istinshaq.
نفل (nafl): Voluntary (supererogatory) act of worship.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on mubalaghah for a person who is fasting a voluntary (nafl) fast?
A) Sunnah
B) Makruh
C) Haram
D) Mubah

Key Takeaway
Mubalaghah is makruh for the fasting person because it risks breaking the fast, and this applies to both obligatory and voluntary fasts.

Combing the Beard in Wudu: An Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on the sunnah status of combing the beard

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa, Muhammad, and Abu Yusuf on takhlil al-lihyah, explain the dalil for each, and identify the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
Combing the beard: sunnah per Abu Yusuf; fadilah per Abu Hanifa; the mufta bihi is sunnah.

In this passage, we encounter a disagreement among the three great Hanafi imams regarding a minor but frequently asked act of wudu: combing the beard (takhlil al-lihyah). Abu Yusuf holds it to be sunnah, while Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani consider it merely a preferred practice. Understanding how each side argues from the sunnah and why the relied-upon view follows Abu Yusuf sharpens your ability to weigh proofs within the madhhab.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue and the main positions
Spot the ruling being debated: takhlil al-lihyah. Note that the text opens with 'يُسَنُّ فِي الْأَصَحِّ' (it is sunnah in the most correct view) – this signals that the author is presenting the preponderant position first.
The phrase 'في الأصح' tells you there are two views and one is stronger.
2
Follow the proof of Abu Yusuf
Read the hadith quoted from Abu Dawud: the Prophet combed his beard and said 'My Lord commanded me.' Abu Yusuf takes this as an explicit command indicating sunnah.
The command 'أمرني ربي' is the key istidlal.
3
Analyse the counter-argument of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad
Their objection: the Prophet did not always do this act. They interpret his action as a demonstration of permissibility (bayan al-jawaz), not as a regular sunnah.
The phrase 'لعدم أنه فعل كذلك' (because he did not always do it) is their reasoning.
4
Understand the tarjih (preponderance)
The commentator sides with Abu Yusuf ('في الأصح'), meaning the relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that combing the beard is sunnah. However, he also notes that one who omits it 'misses the complete sunnah', implying it is not an absolute wajib.
The text says 'لكن يفوته إكمال السنة' – this nuance confirms that even the sunnah view does not make it obligatory.
5
Grasp the thamarah al-khilaf (practical difference)
If a person omits combing the beard, does he lose a sunnah? According to Abu Yusuf, yes; according to Abu Hanifa/Muhammad, he only loses a fadilah. In practice, a Hanafi should prefer to do it to follow the stronger view.
The mufta bihi is sunnah, so it is recommended to do it regularly.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
و) يسن في الأصح (تخليل اللحية الكثة) وهو قول أبي يوسف لرواية أبي داود عن أنس: أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم كان يخلل لحيته والتخليل تفريق الشعر من جهة الأسفل إلى فوق ويكون بعد غسل الوجه ثلاثاً) (لكف أسفلها لأنّ النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم كان إذا توضأ أخذ كفاً. ماء تحت حنكه فخلل به لحيته وقال بهذا أمرني ربي عز وجل، وأبو حنيفة ومحمد يفضلانه لعدم أنه فعل كذلك، لكن يفوته إكمال السنة وأحسن ما يقال في فعله ذلك أنه لبيان الجواز كما في العيني على البخاري
And it is sunnah according to the most correct view to comb the thick beard. This is the statement of Abu Yusuf due to the narration of Abu Dawud from Anas that the Prophet used to comb his beard. Combing is separating the hairs from the bottom upwards, and it is done after washing the face three times. (With a handful of water from below his chin) because the Prophet, when he performed wudu, took a handful of water under his chin and combed his beard with it, and said, 'My Lord commanded me to do this.' Abu Hanifa and Muhammad consider it preferable but not sunnah, because he did not do it consistently. However, he misses the complete sunnah, and the best that can be said about his action is that it was to show permissibility, as in al-Ayni on al-Bukhari.
Source pages p. 70

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding combing the beard (takhlil al-lihyah) during wudu. Abu Yusuf considers it sunnah based on the hadith that the Prophet combed his beard and said his Lord commanded him. Abu Hanifa and Muhammad consider it preferable (fadilah) but not established as sunnah because the Prophet did not do it consistently, and their view suggests it is merely a demonstration of permissibility. The correct view according to the hashiya is the first (sunniyyah) as it says 'في الأصح' (in the most correct view). The commentary also notes that if one does not comb the beard, he misses the complete sunnah.

Key Terms
تخليل اللحية (takhlil al-lihyah): Combing the beard by passing water through it during wudu.
الكثة (al-kaththa): Thick beard; the combing is only for a thick beard, not a sparse one.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the most correct view in the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on combing the beard during wudu?
A) Sunnah
B) Fard
C) Wajib
D) Makruh

Key Takeaway
The mufta bihi in the Hanafi school is that combing a thick beard during wudu is sunnah, based on Abu Yusuf's proof, though Abu Hanifa and Muhammad considered it a preferred but non-sunnah act.

Sunnah of Mubalaghah in Madmadah and Istinshaq
Hashiya explaining sunnah of mubalaghah with proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling of mubalaghah (exaggeration) for a non-fasting and fasting person, and explain the proof from hadith.

Core Idea
Mubalaghah is sunnah muakkadah for non-fasting; the fasting person must avoid it.

This passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi explains the ruling on exaggeration in rinsing the mouth and sniffing water. While the hadith commands it, the exception for the fasting person shows it is not obligatory. We will examine the proof and its implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and general ruling
Mubalaghah in madmadah (rinsing mouth) and istinshaq (sniffing water) is sunnah. Locate the statement in the text: '(و) يسن (المبالغة في المضمضة) و(الاستنشاق)'.
2
Understand the extent of exaggeration
For madmadah: reach water to the top of the throat; for istinshaq: above the nasal cartilage.
This is the definition provided in the passage.
3
Identify the exception
The fasting person should not exaggerate to protect the fast. The text states: 'والصائم لا يبالغ فيهما خشية إفساد الصوم'.
4
Examine the hadith proof
The Prophet said: 'بالغ في المضمضة والاستنشاق إلا أن تكون صائماً' (Exaggerate... unless you are fasting). The imperative indicates command, but the exception shows it is not fard.
5
Classify the hukm
In Hanafi usul, the command is interpreted as sunnah muakkadah because the exception proves it is not absolute obligation.
The proof is the hadith itself; no other proof is cited.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بواحدة لعدم انطباق الأنف على باقي الماء بخلاف المضمضة (و) يسن (المبالغة في المضمضة) وهو إيصال الماء لرأس الحلق (و) المبالغة في (الاستنشاق) وهي إيصاله إلى ما فوق المارن (لغير الصائم والصائم لا يبالغ فيهما خشية إفساد الصوم لقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام: (بالغ) في المضمضة والاستنشاق إلا أن تكون صائماً» (و) يسن في الأصح (تخليل اللحية الكثة) وهو قول أبي يوسف لرواية أبي داود عن أنس: أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم كان يخلل لحيته والتخليل تفريق الشعر من جهة الأسفل إلى فوق ويكون بعد غسل الوجه ثلاثاً) (لكف أسفلها لأنّ النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم كان إذا توضأ أخذ كفاً من ماء تحت حنكه فخلل به لحيته وقال بهذا أمرني ربي عز وجل، وأبو حنيفة ومحمد يفضلانه لعدم المواظبة، ولأنه لإكمال الفرض وداخلها ليس محلاً له بخلاف تخليل الأصابع ورجح في المبسوط قول أبي يوسف رواية أنس رضي الله عنه (و) يسن (تخليل الأصابع) كلها للأمر به ولقوله : من لم يخلل أصابعه بالماء خللها الله بالنار يوم القيامة وكيفيته في اليدين إدخال بعضها في بعض وفي الرجلين بأصبع من يده ويكفي عنه إدخالها في الماء الجاري ونحوه» (و) يسن (تثليث الغسل) فمن زاد أو نقص فقد تعدى وظلم كما ورد في السنة إلا لضرورة بأن زاد لطمأنينة قلبه عن الشك، فلا بأس به لما ورد: دع ما يريبك إلى ما لا يريبك وما قيل إنه لو زاد بنية وضوء آخر لا بأس به أيضاً لأنه نور على نور منعه في البحر بأن تكرار الوضوء في مجلس واحد قبل أن يؤدي بالأول عبادة مقصودة من شرعه كالصلاة وسجدة التلاوة ومس المصحف، كما ذكره الحلبي مكروه لأنه إسراف محض، وقوله في النهر : يحمل عدم الكراهة على الإعادة مرة والكراهة على التكرار مراراً بعيد جداً ولم يقل به أحد أفاده بعض الأفاضل هذا ضرورة الزيادة، وضرورة النقص بأن لا يجد ما يكفي التثليث، وقيد بالغسل لأن المسح لا يسن تكراره عندنا كما في الفتح وفي الخانية، وعندنا لو ثلاث مرات بثلاث مياه لا يكره ولكن لا يكون سنة ولا أدباً قال في البحر: وهو أولى
With one [handful] because the nose does not cover the rest of the water unlike the mouth. (And) it is Sunnah (to exaggerate in rinsing the mouth) which is to reach water to the top of the throat, (and) exaggeration in (sniffing water) which is to reach it above the cartilage of the nose (for a non-fasting person, and a fasting person does not exaggerate in them for fear of spoiling the fast due to his saying, peace be upon him: 'Exaggerate in rinsing the mouth and sniffing water unless you are fasting'). (And) it is Sunnah according to the most correct view (to comb the thick beard) - this is the saying of Abu Yusuf due to the narration of Abu Dawud from Anas that the Prophet (peace be upon him) used to comb his beard. The combing is to separate the hair from the lower side upwards, and it is done after washing the face three times. (With a handful of water under his chin) because the Prophet (peace be upon him), when he performed wudu, took a handful of water under his chin and combed his beard with it and said: 'My Lord, the Exalted, commanded me with this.' And Abu Hanifa and Muhammad prefer leaving it due to lack of continuity and because it is for completing the obligatory act, and the interior of the beard is not a place for it, unlike combing the fingers. And in al-Mabsut, the saying of Abu Yusuf is preferred due to the narration of Anas (may Allah be pleased with him). (And) it is Sunnah (to comb all the fingers) due to the command for it and his saying: 'Whoever does not comb his fingers with water will have them combed by fire on the Day of Judgment.' Its manner in the hands is to interlace one into the other, and in the feet to use one finger of his hand, and it suffices to put them in running water and the like. (And) it is Sunnah (to wash three times). Whoever increases or decreases has transgressed and wronged as reported in the Sunnah, except for necessity: if he increases for tranquility of heart due to doubt, then it is fine due to the report: 'Leave what makes you doubt for what does not make you doubt.' And what is said that if he increases with the intention of another wudu it is also fine because it is light upon light - this is prevented in al-Bahr because repeating wudu in one sitting before performing a worship intended by it like prayer, prostration of recitation, and touching the mushaf, as mentioned by al-Halabi, is disliked because it is pure waste. And his saying in al-Nahr: that the absence of dislike is carried on repeating once, and dislike on repeating multiple times is very far-fetched and no one said it, as some advanced scholars have benefited. This is the necessity of increase. And the necessity of decrease is when one does not find enough for three washings. And it is restricted to washing because wiping is not Sunnah to repeat according to us as in al-Fath and al-Khaniyya. And according to us, if one does three times with three waters it is not disliked but is not Sunnah or proper. Al-Bahr said: it is better.
Source pages p. 70

Commentary
This passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi is a critical refinement of the sharh of Maraqi al-Falah. It addresses four sunnah acts of wudu: exaggeration in rinsing the mouth and sniffing water, combing the thick beard, combing the fingers and toes, and washing each limb three times. The author follows the order of the matn, explaining each ruling with its proof and discussing intra-Hanafi differences where they occur. For exaggeration in mouth and nose rinsing, the hadith explicitly commands it except for the fasting person, establishing it as Sunnah. The exception for the fasting person is to protect the fast. For beard combing, the passage presents a dispute: Abu Yusuf deems it Sunnah based on the Prophet's practice, while Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani do not because they see it as a completion of the washing of the face, and the interior of the beard is not a locus of the obligation; hence it is not Sunnah. Al-Marghinani in al-Hidayah prefers Abu Yusuf's view. For finger combing, the hadith threat ('comb with fire') indicates its importance. For triple washing, the matn states that increasing or decreasing is transgression, but the hashya clarifies that this applies to normal circumstances; increasing for doubt or decreasing due to lack of water is permissible. The ruling is restricted to washing (ghusl) as opposed to wiping (mash), which is not repeated in the Hanafi school. The commentary consistently uses Hanafi authorities like al-Fath, al-Nahr, and al-Bahr to support the positions.

Key Terms
المبالغة (al-mubalaghah): Exaggeration in rinsing the mouth and sniffing water, meaning reaching water to the top of the throat and above the nasal cartilage.
المضمضة (al-madmadah): Rinsing the mouth with water.
الاستنشاق (al-istinshaq): Drawing water into the nose.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which of the following is NOT appropriate when a fasting person performs wudu?
A) He should not exaggerate in madmadah
B) He should not exaggerate in istinshaq
C) He should use a small amount of water to avoid swallowing
D) He must skip the sunnah acts entirely

Key Takeaway
Mubalaghah is sunnah for non-fasting; the fasting person must avoid it to protect the fast.

Beard Combing (Takhlil al-Lihyah) – Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Hashiya presenting intra-Hanafi dispute on beard combing

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on beard combing, cite the proofs of Abu Yusuf and the Sahibayn, and state the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
Beard combing is sunnah according to the most correct Hanafi view, despite disagreement.

This passage presents an internal Hanafi ikhtilaf regarding combing the thick beard during wudu. Abu Yusuf considers it sunnah, while Abu Hanifa and Muhammad do not. We examine the proofs and the tarjih that settles the matter.

Guided Path
1
State the two positions
Abu Yusuf: it is sunnah. Abu Hanifa and Muhammad: it is not sunnah; it is merely permissible or may be left.
The text says: 'وأبو حنيفة ومحمد يفضلانه' – they prefer leaving it.
2
Identify the proofs for each side
Abu Yusuf cites the hadith that the Prophet used to comb his beard and said 'My Lord commanded me with this.' The Sahibayn argue lack of continuous practice and that the interior of the beard is not part of the face for fard washing.
The hadith is from Abu Dawud.
3
Analyze the tarjih
Al-Mabsut prefers Abu Yusuf's view due to the authentic narration of Anas. The phrase 'في الأصح' indicates it is the relied-upon position.
The text says: 'ورجح في المبسوط قول أبي يوسف'.
4
Determine the mufta bihi
The mufta bihi position is that beard combing is sunnah. This is the view applied in fatwa.
This is based on the tarjih of later Hanafi authorities.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

For triple washing, the matn states that increasing or decreasing is transgression, but the hashya clarifies that this applies to normal circumstances; increasing for doubt or decreasing due to lack of water is permissible. The commentary consistently uses Hanafi authorities like al-Fath, al-Nahr, and al-Bahr to support the positions.

Key Terms
تخليل اللحية (takhlil al-lihyah): Combing the thick beard by passing wet fingers through it from underneath upwards.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Finger Combing and Triple Washing: Rulings and Exceptions
Hashiya explaining sunnah of finger combing and triple washing with exceptions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the rulings on finger combing and triple washing, identify exceptions for necessity, and explain the Hanafi position on repeating wudu.

Core Idea
Finger combing is sunnah with a stern warning; triple washing is sunnah but exceptions exist for necessity.

This passage concludes the sunnah acts of wudu with finger combing and triple washing. It also discusses exceptions: increasing washes due to doubt, decreasing due to lack of water, and the ruling on repeating wudu. We will analyze each element.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling on finger combing
It is sunnah to comb between all fingers and toes. The proof is the hadith warning of punishment by fire.
The text says: '(و) يسن (تخليل الأصابع) كلها'.
2
Learn the method
For hands: interlace fingers. For feet: use the little finger of the hand. Putting feet in running water also suffices.
The text describes the manner.
3
State the ruling on triple washing
It is sunnah to wash each limb three times. Increasing or decreasing is transgression unless for necessity.
The text says: '(و) يسن (تثليث الغسل) فمن زاد أو نقص فقد تعدى وظلم'.
4
Understand the necessity exceptions
Increase: if for tranquility of heart due to doubt, it is permissible. But doing a second wudu before performing an act of worship is disliked. Decrease: if insufficient water, one may do less than three.
The text discusses both cases.
5
Note the ruling on wiping
The sunnah of triple washing applies only to washing (ghusl), not to wiping (mash). Wiping is not repeated in the Hanafi school.
The text says: 'وقيد بالغسل لأن المسح لا يسن تكراره عندنا'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

With one [handful] because the nose does not cover the rest of the water unlike the mouth. (And) it is Sunnah (to exaggerate in rinsing the mouth) which is to reach water to the top of the throat, (and) exaggeration in (sniffing water) which is to reach it above the cartilage of the nose (for a non-fasting person, and a fasting person does not exaggerate in them for fear of spoiling the fast due to his saying, peace be upon him: 'Exaggerate in rinsing the mouth and sniffing water unless you are fasting'). (And) it is Sunnah according to the most correct view (to comb the thick beard) - this is the saying of Abu Yusuf due to the narration of Abu Dawud from Anas that the Prophet (peace be upon him) used to comb his beard. The combing is to separate the hair from the lower side upwards, and it is done after washing the face three times. (With a handful of water under his chin) because the Prophet (peace be upon him), when he performed wudu, took a handful of water under his chin and combed his beard with it and said: 'My Lord, the Exalted, commanded me with this.' And Abu Hanifa and Muhammad prefer leaving it due to lack of continuity and because it is for completing the obligatory act, and the interior of the beard is not a place for it, unlike combing the fingers. And in al-Mabsut, the saying of Abu Yusuf is preferred due to the narration of Anas (may Allah be pleased with him). (And) it is Sunnah (to comb all the fingers) due to the command for it and his saying: 'Whoever does not comb his fingers with water will have them combed by fire on the Day of Judgment.' Its manner in the hands is to interlace one into the other, and in the feet to use one finger of his hand, and it suffices to put them in running water and the like. (And) it is Sunnah (to wash three times). Whoever increases or decreases has transgressed and wronged as reported in the Sunnah, except for necessity: if he increases for tranquility of heart due to doubt, then it is fine due to the report: 'Leave what makes you doubt for what does not make you doubt.' And what is said that if he increases with the intention of another wudu it is also fine because it is light upon light - this is prevented in al-Bahr because repeating wudu in one sitting before performing a worship intended by it like prayer, prostration of recitation, and touching the mushaf, as mentioned by al-Halabi, is disliked because it is pure waste. And his saying in al-Nahr: that the absence of dislike is carried on repeating once, and dislike on repeating multiple times is very far-fetched and no one said it, as some advanced scholars have benefited. This is the necessity of increase. And the necessity of decrease is when one does not find enough for three washings. And it is restricted to washing because wiping is not Sunnah to repeat according to us as in al-Fath and al-Khaniyya. And according to us, if one does three times with three waters it is not disliked but is not Sunnah or proper. Al-Bahr said: it is better.
Source pages p. 70

Commentary
This passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi is a critical refinement of the sharh of Maraqi al-Falah. It addresses four sunnah acts of wudu: exaggeration in rinsing the mouth and sniffing water, combing the thick beard, combing the fingers and toes, and washing each limb three times. The author follows the order of the matn, explaining each ruling with its proof and discussing intra-Hanafi differences where they occur. For exaggeration in mouth and nose rinsing, the hadith explicitly commands it except for the fasting person, establishing it as Sunnah. The exception for the fasting person is to protect the fast. For beard combing, the passage presents a dispute: Abu Yusuf deems it Sunnah based on the Prophet's practice, while Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani do not because they see it as a completion of the washing of the face, and the interior of the beard is not a locus of the obligation; hence it is not Sunnah. Al-Marghinani in al-Hidayah prefers Abu Yusuf's view. For finger combing, the hadith threat ('comb with fire') indicates its importance. For triple washing, the matn states that increasing or decreasing is transgression, but the hashya clarifies that this applies to normal circumstances; increasing for doubt or decreasing due to lack of water is permissible. The ruling is restricted to washing (ghusl) as opposed to wiping (mash), which is not repeated in the Hanafi school. The commentary consistently uses Hanafi authorities like al-Fath, al-Nahr, and al-Bahr to support the positions.

Key Terms
تخليل الأصابع (takhlil al-asabi'): Combing the fingers and toes by passing water between them.
تثليث الغسل (tathleeth al-ghusl): Washing each limb three times.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Mustahabb (recommended)
B) Makruh (disliked)
C) Haram (forbidden)
D) Mubah (permissible without dislike)

Key Takeaway
Finger combing and triple washing are sunnah, but necessity exceptions apply; repeating wudu is disliked.

Tahlil al-Asabi' in Wudu: Ruling, Proof, and Method
Ruling on tahlil with proof and method

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on tahlil al-asabi' during wudu, cite the hadith evidence, and explain the method recommended for hands and feet.

Core Idea
Tahlil al-asabi' is sunnah, not wajib; a stern hadith warns but ahad proofs cannot establish obligation.

In this lesson, we examine the act of interlacing fingers (tahlil al-asabi') during wudu. The Hanafi school considers it a strongly recommended practice (sunnah muakkadah), supported by a direct command and a hadith. We will explore the evidence, the prescribed method, and the circumstances under which manual tahlil may be dispensed with.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Its Ruling
Determine what act is being discussed and its legal classification. The text explicitly states 'yusann' (it is sunnah), so tahlil is recommended, not obligatory.
The ruling is derived from the Arabic verb 'yusann' which indicates a sunnah act in fiqh terminology.
2
Locate the Dalil (Evidence)
Find the proof cited: a hadith of the Prophet (peace be upon him) warning those who neglect tahlil. Also, a general command to perform tahlil is mentioned.
The hadith is ahad (solitary), which affects its epistemological weight.
3
Analyze the Wajh al-Dalalah (How the Proof Establishes the Ruling)
Explain how the hadith proves sunnah and not wajib. The threat ('will interlace with fire') shows severe discouragement of omission, but since the hadith is ahad, it cannot establish obligation (wujub) in Hanafi usul.
Zanni al-thubut proofs yield zanni rulings; sunnah is a zanni level of recommendation.
4
Describe the Method (Kayfiyya)
For hands: intertwine the fingers. For feet: use the little finger (of the left hand) starting from the right little toe. Alternatively, inserting the feet into running or abundant moving water suffices.
The method ensures water reaches between all digits.
5
Understand the Expansion (Sharah of 'wa nahwihi')
The text says 'and the like' refers to abundant water (like a tank). In still abundant water, movement is needed to replace tahlil; in running water, the force naturally separates the toes.
This expansion by al-Tahtawi clarifies the conditions for substitution.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
و) يسن (تخليل الأصابع) كلها للأمر به ولقوله : من لم يخلل أصابعه بالماء خللها الله بالنار يوم القيامة وكيفيته في اليدين إدخال بعضها في بعض وفي الرجلين بأصبع من يده ويكفي عنه إدخالها في الماء الجاري ونحوه» قوله: (ونحوه) قال في الشرح : وما هو في حكمه اهـ أي وهو الماء الكثير، والظاهر أنه في الماء الكثير الراكد لا يقوم مقام التخليل إلا بالتحريك وحينئذ فلا فرق بين القليل والكثير بخلاف الجاري لأنه بقوته يدخل الأثناء
And it is sunnah to interlace all the fingers, due to the command and his saying: 'Whoever does not interlace his fingers with water, Allah will interlace them with fire on the Day of Resurrection.' Its manner for the hands is inserting some into others, and for the feet is with the little finger of his hand, and it suffices instead to insert them into running water and the like. His statement: 'and the like' – he said in al-Sharh: 'what is in its ruling,' i.e., abundant water. Apparently, in still abundant water, it does not substitute for tahlil except by moving, and then there is no difference between little and much water, unlike running water because its force enters the gaps.
Source pages p. 71

Commentary
This passage presents the ruling on tahlil al-asabi' (interlacing fingers) during wudu. The author states it is sunnah based on two proofs: the general command from the Prophet (peace be upon him) and a specific hadith warning against neglect. The method is described: for the hands, intertwine the fingers; for the feet, use the little finger of the left hand starting from the right little toe and ending with the left little toe, as detailed in the commentary. Alternatively, inserting the feet into running or abundant water suffices if the water penetrates between the toes. The commentary clarifies that 'like' refers to abundant water; for still water, movement is needed to achieve the effect.

Key Terms
تخليل الأصابع (tahlil al-asabi'): The act of passing water between the fingers/toes during wudu, specifically by interlacing fingers or using the little finger for feet.

Key Takeaway

Tathlith al-Ghusl (Washing Three Times) in Wudu
Ruling on tathlith with exceptions for necessity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on tathlith al-ghusl, distinguish between the fard (first) and sunnah (second and third) washes, and identify valid exceptions for increase or decrease.

Core Idea
Washing three times is sunnah muakkadah; first wash fard, next two sunnah – increasing or decreasing is transgression unless necessary.

This passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi clarifies the Hanafi ruling on washing each limb three times during wudu. It establishes the default sunnah status, warns against deviation as transgression, and outlines legitimate exceptions for necessity. Understanding this distinction prevents common errors in practice and ensures one follows the sunnah correctly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the default ruling
Recognize that tathlith (washing three times) is sunnah muakkadah according to the Hanafi school. The first wash of each limb is fard (obligatory), while the second and third are sunnah.
The hadith of 'two folds of reward' supports the independent reward for the second wash.
2
Distinguish fard vs sunnah
Understand that only the first wash is a pillar (rukn) of wudu; the second and third are not pillars but emphasized sunnah. Missing them does not invalidate wudu but loses reward.
3
Note the prohibition of increase/decrease
The text explicitly states that whoever increases or decreases (beyond three) has transgressed and wronged, based on the Sunnah. This applies unless a valid necessity exists.
4
Recognize valid exceptions
Necessity includes: doubting the completion of washing (increase to remove doubt) – allowed based on 'Leave what makes you doubt'; water scarcity (decrease) – allowed if insufficient water for three. Increasing with intention of separate wudu before performing an act is debated and generally considered makruh.
The increase must be for genuine doubt, not extravagance.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
و) يسن (تثليث الغسل) فمن زاد أو نقص فقد تعدى وظلم كما ورد في السنة إلا لضرورة بأن زاد لطمأنينة قلبه عن الشك، فلا بأس به لما ورد: دع ما يريبك إلى ما لا يريبك وقيل إنه لو زاد بنية وضوء آخر لا بأس به أيضاً لأنه نور على نور منعه في البحر بأن تكرار الوضوء في مجلس واحد قبل أن يؤدي بالأول عبادة مقصودة من شرعه كالصلاة وسجدة التلاوة ومس المصحف، كما ذكره الحلبي مكروه لأنه إسراف محض، وقوله في النهر : يحمل عدم الكراهة على الإعادة مرة والكراهة على التكرار مراراً بعيد جداً ولم يقل به أحد أفاده بعض الأفاضل هذا ضرورة الزيادة، وضرورة النقص بأن لا يجد ما يكفي التثليث، وقيد بالغسل لأن المسح لا يسن تكراره عندنا كما في الفتح وفي الخانية، وعندنا لو ثلاث مرات بثلاث مياه لا يكره ولكن لا يكون سنة لا أدباً قال في البحر: وهو أولى
And it is sunnah to triple the washing. Whoever increases or decreases has transgressed and wronged, as reported in the Sunnah, except for necessity: e.g., he increases for reassurance of his heart due to doubt, then there is no harm because of the hadith: 'Leave what makes you doubt for what does not make you doubt.' And it was said that if he increases with the intention of another wudu, it is also permissible because it is light upon light. Al-Bahr prevented this, saying that repeating wudu in one sitting before performing a prescribed act like prayer, prostration of recitation, or touching the mushaf, as mentioned by al-Halabi, is makruh because it is pure extravagance. Al-Nahr's statement that the absence of karahah applies to one repetition and karahah to multiple repetitions is very far-fetched, and no one has said it, according to some scholars. This is the necessity of increase. And the necessity of decrease is when he does not find enough water for triple. And it is restricted to washing because wiping is not sunnah to repeat in our school, as in al-Fath and al-Khaniyah. And in our school, if he does it three times with three waters, it is not makruh but it is not sunnah or adab. Al-Bahr said: and this is preferable.
Source pages p. 71

Commentary
This passage discusses the ruling on tathlith al-ghusl (washing three times) during wudu. The author confirms it is sunnah, based on the Sunnah. The first wash is considered fard (obligatory), while the second and third are sunnah muakkadah (emphasized). The text warns against increasing or decreasing beyond three, labeling it as transgression ('tada' and 'zulm') except in cases of necessity. Necessity includes increasing due to doubt for reassurance (based on the hadith 'da' ma yuribuk'), or decreasing due to water scarcity. However, the commentary discusses a dispute: some allow increasing with the intention of a separate wudu, but al-Bahr considers it makruh if done in one sitting before performing a prescribed act, as it is extravagance. The restriction applies only to washing, not to wiping (mash), which is not repeated. If one uses three different waters, it is not makruh but also not sunnah or adab. The preferred view is that increasing is only permissible for necessity.

Key Terms
تثليث الغسل (tathlith al-ghusl): Washing each limb three times during wudu, with the first being fard and the next two sunnah muakkadah.
ضرورة (darurah): Necessity that permits deviation from the sunnah, such as water scarcity (decrease) or doubt (increase).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Permissible (mubah)
B) Sunnah
C) Makruh (disliked) – a transgression
D) Haram

Key Takeaway
Tathlith is sunnah muakkadah; the first wash is fard, the second and third are sunnah; deviation without necessity is transgression.

Wiping the Head and Ears in Hanafi Wudu
Rulings on wiping the head and ears in wudu

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on wiping the head and ears during wudu, identify the proof from the Prophet's action, and distinguish sunnah from fard obligations.

Core Idea
Wiping the entire head once is sunnah, not fard, because the Prophet's practice indicates ease, not obligation.

This lesson examines the Hanafi position on wiping the head and ears in wudu. While some schools consider wiping part of the head as obligatory, the Hanafi school considers covering the entire head once as sunnah. The key distinction lies in the nature of wiping (mash) as a light purification, as seen in the Prophet's action. Understanding this ruling helps clarify the difference between obligatory and recommended acts in wudu.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what is being ruled upon (wiping the head and ears) and the legal classification (sunnah). Note that it is not fard or wajib.
The text uses the term 'yusannu' (it is sunnah) explicitly.
2
Locate the dalil
Identify the proof cited: the action of the Prophet (peace be upon him) as narrated by Abdullah ibn Zayd.
The proof is a hadith (sunna ahad) which is zanni al-thubut, supporting the sunnah level.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Explain how the Prophet's action indicates sunnah: his consistent practice without rebuking omission shows it is not obligatory.
The analogy with wiping the splint (jabirah) and tayammum reinforces that wiping is for lightness.
4
Note the inter-madhhab ikhtilaf
Recognize that the Shafi'i school considers wiping part of the head as fard, based on their interpretation of the verse 'wa imsahu bi ru'usikum'.
The practical difference is that in Hanafi, if one omits wiping the head entirely, wudu is still valid but missing a sunnah; in Shafi'i, wudu is invalid.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
Understand why the Hanafi position is mufta bihi: the Prophet's action shows it is sunnah, and the burden of proof for obligation is not met.
Al-Tahtawi notes that al-Burhan preferred the narration of one wipe over three, settling the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
و) يسن (استيعاب الرأس بالمسح) كما فعله النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم (مرة) كمسح الجبيرة والتيمم لأن وضعه للتخفيف (و) يسن (مسح الأذنين ولو بماء الرأس) لأنه غرف غرفة فمسح بها رأسه وأذنيه فإن أخذ لهما ماء جديد بقاء البلة كان حسنا
And it is sunnah to cover the entire head in wiping once, as the Prophet (peace be upon him) did, like wiping the splint and tayammum, because wiping is for lightness. And it is sunnah to wipe the ears, even with the water of the head, because he took a handful, wiped his head and ears with it. If he takes new water for both while the moisture remains, it is good.
Source pages p. 72

Commentary
This passage presents the rulings on wiping the head and ears during wudu. The author states that it is sunnah to cover the entire head in wiping, and this is done once, not three times. The comparison with wiping the splint (jabirah) and tayammum emphasizes that wiping is a form of light purification, so repetition is not required. The method for wiping the head is described elsewhere: place both palms on the front of the head and draw them to the nape and back. For the ears, the sunnah is to wipe them with the same water used for the head, but taking new water while moisture remains is also acceptable. The commentary notes that the preferred method is to wipe the outer ears with the thumbs and inner ears with the index fingers, with the little fingers entering the ear holes.

Key Terms
استيعاب الرأس بالمسح (isti'ab al-ra's bi al-mash): Covering the entire head with wet hands during wiping, performed once.
مسح الأذنين (mash al-udhnayn): Wiping the ears during wudu, preferably with the same water used for the head.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Once
B) Three times
C) Until dry
D) Twice

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, covering the entire head once during wudu is sunnah, and wiping the ears is also sunnah using the same water.

6 min
Al-Dalk and Al-Wala': Sunnah Acts of Wudu
Sunnah rulings on rubbing and sequence in wudu.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling of dalk and wala' in the Hanafi school and explain why they are sunnah rather than fard.

Core Idea
Rubbing and maintaining sequence in wudu are sunnah, not fard—omission does not invalidate wudu.

In wudu, some acts are essential (fard), while others are recommended (sunnah). Two such sunnah acts are rubbing the limbs after washing (dalk) and washing in sequence without delay (wala'). The Hanafi school, based on the Prophet's consistent practice, treats these as meritorious but not obligatory, differing from other schools like the Maliki and Shafi'i.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling of dalk
Read the source text to find the explicit ruling for dalk. Note the Arabic phrase 'yusann' indicating sunnah.
Dalk is sunnah, done after washing the limb by passing the hand over it.
2
Identify the ruling of wala'
Similarly, find the ruling for wala' in the text. Understand its definition: washing the next limb before the previous one dries under normal conditions.
Wala' is sunnah, proven by the Prophet's constant practice (muwazabah).
3
Understand the cross-madhhab difference
Compare the Hanafi view with other schools: Malik and al-Awza'i consider dalk a condition (shart) for wudu; Shafi'is consider wala' fard. Note the practical consequence: for Hanafis, omitting these does not affect validity.
The Hanafi position is supported by the Prophet's practice and the absence of explicit command.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
و) يسن (الدلك) مع لفعله بعد الغسل بأمر أريده على الأعضاء (و) يسن (الولاء) لمواظبته وهو بكسر الواو المتابعة بغسل الأعضاء قبل جفاف السابق مع الاعتدال جسدا وزماناً ومكاناً
And it is sunnah to rub after washing, by doing it after the washing with an action he desires on the limbs. And it is sunnah the sequence due to his constant practice, and it is with kasr of the waw, the following: washing the limbs before the previous one dries, with moderation in body, time, and place.
Source pages p. 72

Commentary
This passage covers two sunnah acts of wudu: dalk (rubbing) and wala' (sequence). Dalk means passing the hand over the washed limb while water is still flowing, and it is sunnah, not fard, contrary to the view of Malik and al-Awza'i who consider it a condition for validity. The act of rubbing is done after washing, by moving the hand over the limb. Wala' refers to washing the next limb before the previous one becomes dry, under normal conditions of body, time, and place. It is sunnah because the Prophet (peace be upon him) consistently observed it. The sequence is not obligatory; if one delays until dryness, the wudu is still valid but the sunnah is missed.

Key Terms
الدلك (al-dalk): Rubbing the limbs after washing with the hand while water is flowing, as a sunnah act.
الولاء (al-wala'): Sequence in wudu: washing each subsequent limb before the previous one dries, under normal conditions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on rubbing (dalk) the limbs during wudu according to the Hanafi school?
A) Fard
B) Wajib
C) Sunnah
D) Makruh

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, dalk (rubbing) and wala' (sequence) are sunnah acts of wudu—recommended but not obligatory, and omitting them does not invalidate the wudu.

8 min
Masah of the Head: Sunnah Method Once
Ruling on the sunnah method of head wiping with proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi sunnah method for wiping the head in wudu and distinguish it from alternative methods, citing the preferred proof.

Core Idea
Wiping the head once, covering the entire head from front to nape and back, is the confirmed sunnah; three wipes have no basis.

In this lesson, we examine the Hanafi ruling on how to perform the sunnah of wiping the head in wudu. The Hashiya al-Tahtawi clarifies the preferred method based on authentic hadith and refutes alternative practices that some consider sunnah. Understanding this will ensure your wudu follows the established prophetic practice as upheld by the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling level
The act is wiping the head fully (isti'ab). The ruling level is sunnah muakkadah, not fard or wajib.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the hadith of Abdullah ibn Zaid ibn Asim (agreed upon), which describes the Prophet's method.
The specific narration is found in the Muwatta' of Malik via Muhammad al-Shaybani.
3
Understand the method from the dalil
Place both palms on the front of the head, draw them to the nape, then return to the front. Then wipe the ears with the fingers.
This method ensures complete coverage and is the preferred narration (riwayat al-afrad).
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some narrated wiping three times, but the text interprets this as three passes with the same water (not separate wipes). The single wipe is the established sunnah.
Alternative methods (e.g., using three fingers) are criticized as baseless.
5
Confirm the mufta bihi
Imams like al-Zaylai, Qadikhan, and al-Zahidi preferred the single wipe method described above. This is the relied-upon position for practice.
The water used does not become musta'mal because it is necessary for fulfilling the sunnah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويسن استيعاب الرأس بالمسح مرة كمسح الجبيرة والتيمم لأن وضعه للتخفيف. مما الرأس، في المحيط والبدائع أنه يكره ومما في الخلاصة أنه بدعة إذ لا دليل على الكراهة. قوله: (مرة) قال في الهداية وما يروى من التثليث محمول عليه بماء واحد وهو مشروع على ما روى الحسن عن أبي حنيفة رضي الله عنه ورجح في البرهان رواية الأفراد على التثليث، وله كيفيات متعدّدة وردت بها الأحاديث ذكر نبذة منها في البناية، واختار بعض أصحابنا رواية عبد الله بن زيد بن عاصم المتفق عليها وهي بمعنى رواية محمد في موطئه عن مالك مسح من مقدم رأسه حتى ذهب بهما إلى قفاه ثم ردهما إلى المكان الذي منه بدأ، ومن ثم قال الزيلعي : والأظهر أنه يضع كفيه، وأصابعه على مقدم رأسه، ويمدهما إلى قفاه على وجه مستوعب جميع ثم يمسح أذنيه بإصبعيه اهـ واختاره قاضيخان وقال الزاهدي هكذا روي عن أبي حنيفة ومحمد اهـ قال في الخانية ولا يكون الماء بهذا مستعملاً ضرورة إقامة السنة اهـ وما في الخلاصة وغيرها من أنه يضع على مقدم رأسه من كل يد ثلاثة أصابع ويمسك إبهاميه وسبابتيه ويجافي بطن كفيه ثم يضع كفيه على جانبي رأسه ففيه تكلف ومشقة كما في الخانية، بل قال الكمال: لا أصل له في السنة. قوله : (كمسح الجبيرة، والتيمم أي والخف فإنه لا يسن فيه التكرار. قوله: (لأن وضعه أي المسح للتخفيف أي بخلاف الغسل فإنه يثلث للتنظيف.
And it is Sunnah to encompass the head with wiping once, like wiping the splint and tayammum, because its position is for lightening. From the head, in al-Muhit and al-Bada'i that it is disliked, and what is in al-Khulasa that it is an innovation since there is no evidence for dislike. He said: (once) said in al-Hidayah: and what is narrated of three times is carried on one water, and it is legislated according to what al-Hasan narrated from Abu Hanifa, may Allah be pleased with him, and preferred in al-Burhan the narration of single over three times. And it has multiple ways reported in hadiths, a sample mentioned in al-Binaya. And some of our companions chose the narration of Abdullah ibn Zaid ibn Asim agreed upon, which is in the sense of Muhammad's narration in his Muwatta' from Malik: wiping from the front of his head until he took them to his nape then returned them to where he started. Hence al-Zaylai said: the most apparent is that he places his palms and fingers on his front head and extends them to his nape in a manner encompassing all, then wipes his ears with his two fingers. End. And Qadikhan chose it, and al-Zahidi said: thus it is narrated from Abu Hanifa and Muhammad. End. He said in al-Khaniyya: the water is not thereby used due to necessity of establishing the Sunnah. End. And what is in al-Khulasa and others that he places on his front head from each hand three fingers and holds his thumbs and index fingers and separates his palms then places his palms on his head's sides, therein is effort and hardship as in al-Khaniyya, rather al-Kamal said: it has no basis in the Sunnah. He said: (like wiping the splint, and tayammum) i.e., and the khuff, for no repetition is Sunnah in it. He said: (because its position i.e., wiping is for lightening) i.e., unlike washing for which three times are for cleaning.
Source pages p. 72

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on the Sunnah of wiping the head fully in wudu. The matn states that it is Sunnah to encompass the entire head with wiping once, analogous to wiping over a splint (jabirah) or tayammum, as wiping is meant for ease, unlike washing. The Hashiya then comments. First, it addresses a dispute: whether wiping the head once (as opposed to three times) is disliked or an innovation. The text clarifies that the preferred view is the single wipe, and the narration of three times is interpreted as three passes with the same water. The author then details the method: the preferred way is to place both palms on the front of the head and draw them to the nape, then return, ensuring the entire head is covered. The ears are then wiped with the fingers. Alternative methods (e.g., using three fingers) are criticized as baseless. The Hashiya confirms that the water used does not become 'used' (musta'mal) because this action is necessary for fulfilling the Sunnah. The analogy to splint and tayammum is explained: just as those involve no repetition of wiping, so too head wipe is once. The rationale is that washing is for cleansing (requiring three times), while wiping is for lightening.

Key Terms
استيعاب (isti'ab): To encompass or cover the entire head with wiping
مسح (masah): Wiping with wet hand without flowing water
مرة (marrah): One single wipe, as opposed to three

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hashiya, what is the relied-upon method for wiping the head in wudu?
A) Wipe with three fingers from each hand, separate palms, then wipe sides
B) Place both palms on the front of the head and draw them to the nape, then return, then wipe ears
C) Wipe the head three times with separate water each time
D) Wipe only the front part of the head

Key Takeaway
The sunnah is to wipe the entire head once, from front to back and returning, then wipe the ears; any other method (three times, using three fingers) lacks a sound basis.
